Political Situation in Hungary is Uneasy 40

Conflicting Opinions Among Various Factions on the Issue of Domestic Reform

⊙Budapest, the capital of Hungary, The political situation in Hungary is visibly uneasy. The most important domestic issues are the reform of the land system and the reform of elections. Hungarian political parties have different opinions on these issues and have formed their own factions. As a result, there may be repercussions for the government's position and the form of the National Assembly. Regarding the land system reform plan, the aristocratic party and the large landowners have expressed opposition, while the small farmers' party has expressed support. Prime Minister Gömbös currently has two options: either to make concessions to the aristocratic party and the large landowners so that the government faction can maintain its current majority, or to sacrifice a part of the government faction and rely on the small farmers' party to consolidate itself. Recently, Gömbös gave a speech in Szolnok, vehemently attacking the aristocratic party, but after meeting with Count Károlyi, the leader of the party, at a luncheon in a certain place, the two sides seemed to have reached a compromise. If the aristocratic party's opposition remains strong, Gömbös can still obtain a majority on the side of the small farmers' party. The leader of the party, Eckhardt (i.e., the Hungarian representative to the League of Nations), said that if the government wants to form an alliance with them, it should thoroughly change its policies and form a definite alliance. Regarding the issue of election reform, Eckhardt said, "I and General Gömbös have already agreed in detail, but what the attitude of the small farmers' party will be depends on whether Gömbös can make his party members obey." (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Heavy Snow and Gale in Europe and America 41

London, Paris, and Rome Become Silver Worlds

Plane Crashes and Gold Bars are Found in Two Boxes

Mississippi River Floods Both Banks

(London) Last night, heavy snow continued to fall in many parts of Great Britain, accompanied by strong winds. The wind force was so strong that it reached speeds of up to 86 miles per hour in several places. Farms in Lincolnshire were blocked by wind and snow, cutting off traffic from the outside world. Along the coast, the wind was strong and the waves were raging, and fishing boats hurriedly took refuge in ports. Those who were late were blown ashore. The severe cold raged as far as southern Spain. The whole of France was plunged into wind and snow yesterday. Fishing ports suffered heavy losses. Paris was blocked with snow, and 4,500 people are currently clearing it. Heavy snow fell in Rome and other places. The wind and snow in British Columbia has swept across the United States and reached Mexico. 170 people have died as a result, and those who are missing have not yet been found. The losses amount to five million yuan. The Mississippi River flooded both banks, drowning many people and animals. A black man, regardless of his own danger, repeatedly jumped into the icy water to save lives, and hundreds of people were saved as a result. His courage and righteousness are commendable. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

(London) Yesterday, when a British scheduled airmail plane was flying between London and Paris, the luggage compartment door was blown open by the wind, causing the gold bars on board to fall out. It is now known that these gold bars did not fall into the sea, but fell into the British countryside. This morning at dawn, a large number of police officers searched along the flight route, but there is still no news. It is reported that these gold bars are worth about £22,000. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(London) The Standard Evening News reported that two boxes of gold bars, totaling 16 bars, were found near Gredon, Kent, England, which had fallen out of British airmail plane flying between London and Paris. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

International Commercial Telegram 43

—Reuters Special Commercial Telegram, January 28—

Gold and Silver ▲British Gold The London gold price today was 141 shillings 6 pence, down 2 pence.

▲British Silver In the London silver market today, the United States and China purchased, India bought and resold. The closing market was stable. The spot price was 24.75 pence, and the futures price was 24.875 pence, both up 0.0625.

▲American Silver Canadian silver market, futures trading was quiet, with some contract prices unchanged and others slightly increased.

Exchange Rates

▲British-American In the London foreign exchange market today, due to the gold bar case verdict, it was still uncertain, and the US dollar continued to be in demand. The British-American exchange rate opened at $4.85375, down 625 from the previous US-UK close. It fell 2.75 within an hour after opening to $4.82625, and then rose 375 at noon to $4.83. At 1:00 PM, it continued to rise 875 to $4.83875, and at 6:00 PM, it rose 1.25 to $4.85125. Also, one US dollar is worth 4 shillings 1.471 pence.

▲British-French Opened at 74.78 francs, up 19 bings from Saturday's close. At 11:00 AM, the price was 74.65 francs, down 13 bings from the opening price. This price remained unchanged until 2:00 PM in the afternoon.

Cotton and Wheat ▲American Cotton The cotton market fell due to long covering, but there was some buying after the fall.

▲British Cotton The Liverpool cotton market, the May contract price was 6.79, the same as the previous closing price.

▲British Wheat The Liverpool wheat market, at 1:00 PM today, the May contract price was 5 shillings 1.25 pence, down 25 from Saturday's close. ▲American Wheat The Chicago wheat market, the opening price was slightly lower, due to reports that the weather in the United States is now milder.

Rubber ▲London The London rubber market situation, the opening was quiet, and then turned loose. At noon, the transaction price for the April and June contracts was 6.375 pence, down 0.0625 from Saturday's close.

▲New York The rubber market, the market sentiment remains loose.

Securities ▲New York Before the opening of the New York stock market, a favorable factor for the market was that, according to the steel industry report's estimate, steel mills' work last week accounted for 53% of capacity. However, the recent increase in work was due to a decrease in inventory. Now that inventory is gradually increasing, it is expected that the output will be lower. Steel mills of the Yangtze River type account for 64% of production capacity this week and are expected to increase to 65% within ten days. An unfavorable factor for the market is the uncertainty of the foreign exchange market, which is alarming. This morning, when the stock market opened, various stocks mostly fell slightly. Steel stocks were loose, and merchants were unwilling to buy or sell, wanting to wait for the development of the situation. Securities trading seems likely to remain narrow. The prices are as follows:

Plenary Meeting of the London Chinese Art Exhibition Organizing Committee 44

(Nanjing) The organizing committee of the London Chinese Art Exhibition held a plenary meeting on the 28th, deciding on multiple measures to ensure the safety of transporting antiquities to England. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Panchen Enters Qing During Spring Warmth 45

(Nanjing) The Panchen Lama's office in Nanjing received a telegram from the Panchen Lama's headquarters stating that the Grand Master left Ningxia on the morning of the 26th and arrived at the Alxa Banner Wangfu in the evening, preaching and transforming in Qing during the spring warmth. 160 horses carrying items will arrive in Beijing on the 28th and will be distributed to various dignitaries on the 29th. (Special Telegram, 28th)

(Beiping) The Panchen Lama stayed in Shiweishan on the night of the 21st, departed on the morning of the 22nd, and arrived in Ningxia City that evening, staying for three days. He left Ningxia City on the morning of the 26th and arrived at the Alxa Banner Wangfu at 8:00 PM that evening. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Director of the Ministry of Finance's Tax Department Reports on the Abolition of Excessive and Miscellaneous Taxes 46

(Nanjing) Gao Bingfang, Director of the Ministry of Finance's Tax Department, reported on the abolition of excessive and miscellaneous taxes at the Ministry's weekly memorial service on the 28th. According to reports from various provinces, the types of taxes abolished have reached more than 2,600, amounting to more than 28 million yuan. Of the provincial and local supervisory committees that have been established, there are a total of ten provinces, and the remaining four provinces will also be established separately. As for using stamp tax funds to subsidize remote provinces, such as 15,000 yuan per month for Ningxia and 10,000 yuan per month for Qinghai, they have all been allocated. The authorities in those provinces have also done their best to abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes. (Special Telegram, 28th)

He Yaotsu as Envoy to Turkey 47

Turkey Expresses Great Welcome

(Nanjing) Regarding He Yaotsu as envoy to Turkey, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed Hu Shih-tse, the head of the Office of the Plenipotentiary Representative to the League of Nations, to notify the Turkish government and urge the mutual appointment of ministers to China. Hu telegraphed back that the Turkish Ministry of Foreign Affairs expressed great welcome to Minister He, but the Turkish minister to China may not be appointed until June or July because the Turkish Parliament must hold a meeting in March or April to pass the embassy budget. (Special Telegram, 28th)

North China Water Conservancy Standing Committee Approves Plans for Radically Curing the Yongding River, etc.; Hydraulic Engineering Laboratory Holds Board Meeting in the Afternoon 48

(Tianjin) The North China Water Conservancy Association held a standing committee meeting at 9:00 AM on the 28th. Attendees included Peng Jiqun, Zhang Houwan, Li Shutian, Li Yizhi, Xu Shida, Zhang Boling, Yang Baoling, Zhu Guangcai, Jie, Chen Guansi, and representatives of the construction departments of Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, and Chahar, including Yichao, totaling 16 people. Peng Jiqun chaired the meeting. After reporting on association affairs, the following was resolved: (1) For the plan to radically cure the Yongding River, a barrier dam should be built first. The association will jointly survey the topography of the dam site with the Shanxi Construction Department, send it to the association for design, and then request funds from the Jinghe Association. (2) The project to reduce the flow of the rivers flowing into the sea independently and the methods for recruiting workers will be handled by the standing committee and the Hebei Provincial Government. (3) The Longfeng River control gate plan was approved. The meeting adjourned at noon. At 2:00 PM in the afternoon, the Hydraulic Engineering Laboratory held a board meeting at the association. Li Fudou reported on recent engineering work. At 3:00 PM, the directors went to the work site to inspect the work in person and were very satisfied with the laboratory's engineering work. However, due to the cold weather, it must be extended to March before it can be completed. (Central News Agency Telegram, 28th)

Anti-Drug Movement in Beiping 49

(Beiping) The Beiping Anti-Drug Movement Propaganda Week started on the 28th. The entire city was plastered with anti-drug slogans. The Hebei and Beiping radio stations broadcast anti-drug speeches from 5:30 PM to 6:30 PM. Personnel were dispatched to all movie theaters to give speeches and distribute leaflets on time. From 10:00 AM on the 29th, an anti-drug conference for all circles was held in the Zhongshan Hall of Zhongshan Park. The Municipal Government's Public Security and Health Bureaus reported on the progress of the anti-drug campaign, and the Director of the Health Bureau, Fang Yiji, and others gave academic lectures on drug prevention. On the morning of the 28th, the Municipal Party Headquarters issued a letter to fellow citizens, severely condemning the evils of drugs and expressing hope that fellow citizens would awaken quickly, etc. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

League of Nations Experts Gu De and Others Inspect River Works in Shandong 50

(Jinan) League of Nations experts Gu De, accompanied by committee consultant Pu Deli, technician Zhang Jiong, translator Zhang Xinyuan, Yellow River Commission engineers Su Lansheng, section chief Qi Shou'an, Jihe Bureau chief Hua, and others, arrived from Batou Dong this morning, inspected Huangzhuang, and arrived at Liuzhuang at noon. Zhang Lianjia, director of the Provincial River Bureau, and others arrived early to greet them. Because Liuzhuang is a well-known dangerous work site, it was inspected for a long time. Hua and Qi returned west, and the rest continued east, inspecting dangerous works such as Nankou Huanghuasi Lishengtun. All were carefully inspected. They stayed overnight in Shilibu and planned to inspect Donglai tomorrow morning, arriving in Ji'nan in the afternoon. After resting for a day or two, they will inspect the lower reaches. Because the estuary is not frozen, they cannot go there and will only go to Lijin before returning to Ji'nan to inspect the Xiaoqing River. They are expected to stay in Ji'nan for a week, waiting for Nie Yufu to arrive in Ji'nan from Bian, and then return to Beijing together to inspect the Huai River. They are scheduled to stay in China for three months. Gu and others declined to express their inspection opinions, saying that they would be published after a report was prepared and sent to the League of Nations for transmission to the Economic Committee. When Gu and others inspected Fenglou, Hu Yuanhui, director of the Hebei Construction Department, also accompanied them. Gu said that there were still four outlets flowing at the Jiugu Road breach, one outlet being ten meters wide and eight or nine zhang deep, with a very strong current. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Measures for Blocking Waterways in Eastern Fujian Counties 51

( ) After the victory over the bandits in Eastern Fujian, the authorities decided to implement waterway blockades to assist in the suppression and eradicate the root causes as soon as possible. According to military sources, the authorities have formulated specific measures for blocking waterways in Eastern Fujian counties, and the checkpoints and stopping points for ships have also been designated. These include: Qianqi Shacheng Point, Diantou Bai, Lin'nan Town, Huangqi Xun, Qinyu, Qimen in Fuding; Wuqi Zhixi, Sansha, Hou'ao, Houdun, Yantian in Xiapu; Xietan in Shouning; Shekou, Yangtou Saiqi Xiabaishi, Baima in Fu'an; Xiwei in Ningde. Furthermore, in order to reduce the burden on the people in the newly recovered bandit areas in various counties, the collection of rents and grains is not allowed. The principles are: 1) During the village cleaning period, landlords may not demand rent from tenants; 2) After the village cleaning is completed, the local situation will be investigated and handled appropriately. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Recent News on the International Issues Discussion Group 52

(Nanjing) The International Issues Discussion Group of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has 152 members, 91 internal staff members, and 61 staff members from embassies and consulates. The group has sent a special letter inviting Yan Huiqing, the Ambassador to Russia stationed in Tianjin, to come to Beijing at the beginning of next month to give a lecture. The group's research projects include: 1) International Organizations; 2) International Public and Private Law; 3) Diplomatic Organs; 4) Treaties; 5) China's International Relations; 6) World Politics; 7) International Intelligence; 8) Overseas Chinese Affairs; 9) Others, totaling over 140 items. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Guizhou Provincial Government Requests Funds for Work Relief 55

(Nanjing) The Guizhou Provincial Government, due to the inability to provide relief to the areas in the province affected by bandits, and upon receiving repeated orders from Chairman Chiang to expedite the construction of the Hunan-Guizhou Highway, has telegraphed the Executive Yuan to urgently instruct the Relief Commission to allocate a large sum of money to implement work relief, and to instruct Hunan Province to purchase 40,000 shi of rice to be transported to Guizhou for relief. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Requests a Six-Month Extension for the Term of Inspectors 56

(Nanjing) After the abolishment of the Negotiation Offices in various provinces, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs divided the inspection areas into four regions: 1) Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Sichuan; 2) Shandong, Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu; 3) Zhejiang, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Guizhou; 4) Hebei, Shanxi, Rehe, Chahar, Suiyuan. Each region was assigned one inspection commissioner with a temporary term of six months. Subsequently, the term was extended for eight months. Last July, due to the complexity of negotiations in Chahar, the province was separated from the inspection area and a special commissioner was appointed to handle it. In October, another special commissioner was established in Beiping to handle inspection affairs in Hebei, Shanxi, Rehe, and Suiyuan. Now that the term of the inspectors has expired again, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has recently submitted a request to the Executive Yuan for another six-month extension. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Ministry of Finance's Opinion on Transaction Tax 57

(Nanjing) The Shanghai Stock Exchange Federation enumerated the disadvantages of collecting transaction taxes, which the Executive Yuan submitted to the Ministry of Finance for joint discussion. The Ministry of Finance has now replied, stating that the transaction tax is paid by the buyers and sellers, and the report's assumption that it is borne by the brokers is a fundamental misunderstanding. However, the reasoned arguments in the report are not groundless and should be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for joint review. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Problem of Making Up for Shortfalls in Various Agencies 66

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance sent a letter to the National Government Audit Office yesterday, stating that the shortfalls in various agencies were originally included in the overall budget to offset annual expenditures. The surplus income outside the budget is in fact an absolute minority and cannot be relied upon to offset the national treasury, nor can it be possible to raise funds separately. All shortfalls should be made up by the agencies themselves by vigorously economizing on expenditures, or by the responsible agencies finding ways to allocate funds within their jurisdiction. No further requests should be made to the national treasury to avoid affecting the budget. The letter was sent back for verification. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Japanese and Puppets Jointly Establish Population Registration Office in Gubeikou 69

(Beiping) Gubeikou reports that the Japanese and puppet joint population registration office was established in Gubeikou a few days ago, located on Hedong Street, in the courtyard of the Sakata Group automobile company, named the "Great East Company." Its nature is exactly the same as the Great East Company in Yuguan. All outgoing travelers must first report their name, age, place of origin, occupation, destination, and the number of people in their family in detail to the company, fill out an entry permit, and pay three dimes. Only after the puppet national border police have inspected it will they be allowed to leave the country. There are still inspectors along the way who will inspect it at any time. If there are any errors, they will be detained and subjected to appropriate punishment. Merchants traveling to Rehe all regard it as a difficult road. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Labor Strike at Tianjin Danhua Match Company 72

(Tianjin) Labor strikes in Tianjin this year have been frequent as the lunar new year approached. The problem of layoffs at the Yuyuan Yarn Factory was just resolved by the authorities on the 28th. The Danhua Match Company also had a strike due to demands for increased bonuses. More than a thousand workers went on strike on the morning of the 28th, tightly closing the factory gates and surrounding the manager, creating a very dangerous situation. The authorities dispatched police to suppress the strike and arrested four ringleaders. It was only at night that the situation returned to normal. The factory has now announced that it will be closed for the New Year holiday starting on the 29th, and the bonus issue for workers will be resolved by the authorities in seven days. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Yang Hucheng Will Station Troops in Shang County 73

(Xi'an) Yang Hucheng, stationed in Zhen'an, is supervising the suppression of Xu Haidong's bandit troops. He decided to station troops in Shang County within days to supervise the suppression. In Zhen'an, he summoned officers and soldiers involved in the suppression and gave instructions. Officers who failed to suppress the bandits effectively were punished. Brigade Commander Liu Yanbiao received a major demerit, Regiment Commander Jing Jianye was dismissed and allowed to remain, and Regiment Commander Liu Yunlong was immediately dismissed and handed over to the military law department for severe punishment for dereliction of military discipline. Since Yang announced the punishment of a large number of officers who failed to suppress the bandits effectively, the situation has suddenly become serious. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Relief Supplies for the Remnant Bandits in Southern Anhui Have Been Cut Off 80

The Disaster Situation in Various Counties in Hubei is Severe 83

(Hankou) The Hubei Disaster Relief Association has been receiving telegrams from various counties requesting relief, and the situation is becoming more dire. The number of disaster victims in Qishui has reached 300,000, with families exchanging children to eat. Many disaster victims are filling their stomachs with white clay, tree bark, and grass roots. Those who die of starvation and suicide are appearing in succession. Disaster victims in the provincial capital gathered. Party and government personnel held a review on the 28th, limiting it to three sentences and immediately releasing winter relief. There are nearly 300,000 disaster victims in Hankou, and the Winter Relief Association is scheduled to release relief for three days starting on the 31st. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Guizhou Military and Civilian Joint Celebration Issues Circular Telegram 88

⊙Guiyang (Title Abbreviated) Our country is unfortunate. Communist bandits are rampant. Wherever their evil influence reaches, the people are displaced, fields and houses are ruined, security is disturbed, and the party and the country are harmed more than ever. This time, the Jiangxi bandits fled westward, rushing like wolves and pigs, hoping to unite with the Xu bandits who fled to northern Sichuan and the Xiao He bandits in western Hunan to devastate the southwest. Our central government is concerned about the difficult times and has summoned a large army to pursue and suppress them day and night. Triumphant songs are played repeatedly, and the masses rejoice. Therefore, a Guizhou military and civilian joint celebration will be held on the 25th to connect the feelings between the military and the people and increase their mutual cooperation. However, the major villains and ringleaders are still awaiting public execution. It is hoped that the entire country will unite under the leadership of Chairman Chiang, concentrate its strength, unite the military and the people, thoroughly eliminate the remnant bandits, clarify official administration, and implement the revival of rural areas. Suppressing bandits is for saving the people, and internal stability can resist foreign aggression. Therefore, we will strive for the realization of the Three Principles of the People to achieve the completion of the national revolution. The future of the party and the country depends on it. Guizhou Military and Civilian Joint Celebration. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Military and Financial Affairs in Sichuan Province 98

—Liu Xiang's Report to the Financial Community—

Chongqing Correspondence. During the previous critical military period, there was unease in Sichuan's financial situation. As a result of the authorities' best efforts to provide relief, the situation has recently improved. Liu Xiang, Commander-in-Chief of the Sichuan Bandit Suppression, convened a meeting with the financial community at the United Public Treasury the other day. Chen Shaowei, the Central Sichuan Finance Special Envoy, was also invited to attend. Liu gave a speech on the spot, in addition to announcing measures to reorganize finances, and also gave a very detailed account of the military deployment in eastern and southern Sichuan. The details are divided as follows:

Proper Military Deployment. Liu of Shoushan said in his opening speech: "Since I returned from Beijing, I have had no opportunity to speak with you due to military matters. After two consultations with Special Envoy Chen regarding the financial issues in Sichuan, we have reached considerable solutions. As for military affairs, deployments have been properly completed. These two issues are what I want to talk about today, and I believe they are what you are interested in hearing. First, the military is now properly deployed and there is no other concern.

Measures to Reorganize Finance. Second, regarding the financial situation, the central government attaches great importance to Sichuan's finances and has promised subsidies. Sichuan is very grateful for the central government's care. However, the central government needs to investigate the situation in Sichuan to know the details. Therefore, Special Envoy Chen was specially dispatched to Sichuan to handle everything. In the future, Sichuan's finances will definitely have a complete solution. This can be stated with certainty. Due to the previous serious military situation, many disputes arose in the financial sector of this city due to the soaring of foreign water Shen Hui. Fortunately, with the sympathy and maintenance of all parties, we overcame the difficulties. However, the bandit suppression military operations have not yet been completed, so there will naturally be more problems in the future. If we only care about electing debts, then military expenses will be insufficient. If we only care about military expenses, then we will not be able to consider the losses of creditors. After careful consideration, we have come up with several conditions that are most important: 1) Reorganization of finances. The measures are: 1. Issue long-term public bonds of 120 million yuan. 2. Past debts will be repaid over ten years, interest rates will be reduced, monthly interest will be six li, interest will be paid in July, and principal will be repaid in June. This change is purely due to the bandit suppression military operations and is out of necessity. I hope that all parties will take the overall situation into account and make concessions to maintain it. I will be absolutely responsible. 2) Reorganize local bank notes. The measures are: 1. Local bank notes will not be allowed to be issued from today. Ten-yuan and five-yuan notes will be sealed up. 2. In the future, land bank notes will be used to offset loan certificates, and one thousand yuan of land bank notes will be sealed up. 3. The Finance Department will concentrate cash in other counties to exchange for land bank notes. 4. The Finance Department has been instructed to collect and destroy all ten-yuan and five-yuan notes. This method will be submitted to the central government and it is hoped that it will be adopted. It has been submitted to Special Envoy Chen to report to the central government," he said.

Speech by Special Envoy Chen. After Liu finished speaking, Special Envoy Chen continued to speak, saying that the central government attaches great importance to Sichuan's military and political affairs, and specially dispatched his brother to Sichuan to assist in everything regarding financial issues, and that it will be handled after considering the local situation. The proposed plan will be forwarded to the central government and there will be a complete solution. Then, Liu Hangchen, Director of the Finance Department, expressed his views, and the financial community spoke in succession. The meeting lasted four hours before it adjourned.

Red Cross Society Song Branch Relieves Zhejiang Refugee Transients 99

▲Resolution to Establish a Temporary Shelter

Songjiang Correspondence: The Songjiang branch of the Chinese Red Cross Society held its eighth council meeting on the 27th. Items discussed included: 1) The chairman reported on Zhou Xuewen's proposal to open a shelter to relieve Zhejiang drought-stricken refugee transients, requesting retroactive approval. Resolution: retroactive approval granted. Location decided: Chaoguo Temple. Limit temporarily set at 1,000 people. Time: starting January 31st. Expenses: The branch will advance 1,000 yuan, and Mr. Xu Jingyang, an economic committee member of the branch, will advance one shi of white rice to start operations. Zhou Xuewen will request assistance from the head office and the Relief Committee. 2) Appoint Zhu Guanghan, Yang Bingwen, Du Shiting, Yu Henian, Zheng Hanqing, Qian Jiamin, and Du Lianhua as members of the branch's asset committee. Qu Bingchang, Qian Mingquan, and Xu Jingyang as members of the branch's economic committee. Resolution: passed. 3) Nominations for administrative staff. Resolution: Zhu Jiuwang and Wang Ruozhou were nominated as directors. Huang Xiaohe and Wang Xichuan as clerks. Bai Guanlan, Du Lianhua, Xia Fengchi, Yu Shanjing, Wang Mingfu, and Wu Yinzi as staff members. Staff members will be appointed at the discretion of the directors, and workers will also be hired by the directors. Chen Nianci was appointed as head of publicity, Zhang Shaoxiu and Ke Dehuan as heads of Western medicine, and Xu Jingyang and Xia Jinghan as heads of Traditional Chinese Medicine. Fundraising will be undertaken by members of the branch. 4) Nomination of accounting staff. Resolution: Xia Fengchi was nominated as accountant. 5) Nomination of temporary economic management personnel. Resolution: Du Lianhua and Du Ruozhou nominated to manage. 6) Write letters to the leaders of various agencies and major philanthropists requesting assistance for the branch's shelter for Zhejiang drought-stricken refugee transients. Resolution: Passed.

After the Songjiang branch of the Chinese Red Cross Society resolved to establish a refugee shelter, it also telegraphed the Shanghai office of the National Government Relief Committee, requesting approval for implementation. The telegram is recorded below: "To Chairman Xu Jun of the Shanghai Office of the National Government Relief Committee: In recent times, no fewer than several thousand refugees from Zhejiang, including Xiashi, Wangdian, and Haining Tongxiang, have fled to Songjiang one after another. They are visible everywhere in the streets and alleys. They are starving and freezing, and their condition is miserable. Our association cannot bear to stand by and watch thousands of refugees become homeless, and we fear that undesirable elements may take the opportunity to sneak in, which could jeopardize local security. Therefore, we convened an emergency meeting and, after a public resolution, decided to establish a temporary Zhejiang drought-stricken refugee transit shelter and sent Director Zhou Xuewen to your committee to negotiate. We are deeply grateful that Standing Committee Member Wang Yiting and other committee members agreed to send the refugees onwards. Now, our association has earnestly requested large philanthropists who generously donated to the Bingzi and Dingmao wartime disasters to first find ways to raise funds and start operations. It is scheduled to open a shelter at Chaoguo Temple in Songjiang on the 31st to accommodate refugees. At the same time, our association will conduct separate fundraising activities so that thousands of refugees can escape freezing and starvation. In addition to reporting to the headquarters of the Chinese Red Cross Society, we hereby urgently telegraph your committee to request approval for implementation. We await your orders with utmost urgency. Sheng Yuan, President of the Songjiang Branch of the Chinese Red Cross Society, and Zhu Jiuwang, respectfully. "

Attached is a letter from the Songjiang Branch of the Chinese Red Cross Society: "Dear Editor, In the Songjiang correspondence in your newspaper of January 27th, there is a paragraph that reads: 'Shanghai gentlemen have come to Songjiang to accommodate refugees, and it has been agreed with Shanghai charitable magnates Xu Shiying and Wang Yiting to allocate 10,000 taels of silver.' This does not correspond to the facts. Our branch director Zhou Xuewen contacted Mr. Wang Yiting of Shanghai regarding the issue of future repatriation. The allocation of 10,000 taels of silver is completely untrue. We hereby request a correction. Sincerely, Songjiang Branch of the Chinese Red Cross Society, January 27th."

Songjiang Tinglin Xiahengjing Robbery

Xu Jinsheng's home, a farmer from Qitu, Xiahengjing, Tinglin, was suddenly attacked by more than ten local-speaking bandits armed with shotguns, wooden sticks,刺刀 (bayonets),麻繩 (hemp ropes), and other weapons around midnight on the 25th. They pried open the gate and entered. First, they forced Xu's mother (63 years old) to hand over her hidden silver, but failed and injured her in the process. They then entered each room and robbed eight shi of white rice, two cotton quilts, and many items of clothing, which they loaded onto a boat and escaped. However, because the victim knew that the perpetrators were local bandits, he did not want to cause trouble and did not report the incident. Later, he was pressured by public opinion to report to the First Sub-bureau, requesting that they be apprehended.

Wuxi Telegram Requesting the Cancellation of Silkworm Seed Control

The local Silkworm Seed Industry Association, citing reports that Jiangsu Province has revised its silkworm seed control measures, stating that this year's seed prices will be uniformly set at 6 jiao by the government for factories, and 4 jiao when sold to the public. However, if various farms have the ability to sell to external markets, they may operate freely, selling at 4 jiao within the province, etc. It is clear that the silkworm seed control management measures are beginning to waver. However, the purpose of the control management is to preserve the strength of the people and promote the progress of the domestic silkworm industry, preventing abnormal growth and blind competition among enterprises, based on the absolute unification of production and distribution. If various farms are allowed to sell freely, it will revert to the state of competitive commodity sales and unplanned distribution, and the effectiveness of control management will be lost. Therefore, yesterday, a telegram was sent to the Provincial Government's Department of Construction, requesting that the distribution methods for this year's spring seeds be clearly indicated, and that thorough control management be strictly implemented. If thorough control management cannot be established, the effect of improvement will be difficult to achieve. We hope that the government will save the country's financial resources and explicitly order the cancellation of control management, abolish the Silkworm Industry Improvement Management Committee, and not leave this redundant agency, so that it may be a blessing to the people.

Jiashan Truth of the Gan Yao Massacre

In Xuejiawan, Hedong Dai, Gan Yao Town, Chen, wife of Zhang Kecai from Zhenjiang, 36 years old, rented her womb to Qiu Azhong from Ningbo several years ago to bear a child. She had rented out capital of 200 yuan, which had been redeemed at the expiration of the lease period before the incident. The night before her death, Chen asked her husband for one yuan, but Kecai replied that he had no money, which led to an argument. That night, Chen died tragically. The county court paid close attention to this matter and sent officials to the countryside to examine the body. The examination revealed that the deceased had knife marks on all parts of her head and face, and that her genitals had been cut open with a knife. A bamboo knife stained with blood was found in Zhang Kecai's home. The body has now been discarded next to Qiu Azhong's house. Qiu Azhong and his wife, as well as the deceased's husband, Zhang Kecai, have been escorted to the court for interrogation. The truth will not be difficult to uncover.

Special Article

Enemy or Friend? (3) (Continued) Xu Daolin 100

—An Examination of Sino-Japanese Relations—

—Xu Daolin

(2) The Error of the Asian Monroe Doctrine: A careful observation of Japan's actions over the past three years reveals that the Japanese intend to overcome their domestic difficulties through outward expansion and hegemony. The first step is to achieve the position of absolute ruler of Asia, thereby constantly revealing their aspirations for an East Asian Monroe Doctrine, both internally and externally. However, we ultimately believe that 1935 is different from 1826, when the United States sang the Monroe Doctrine. Not only is the era different, but the situation is also completely different. Because Britain and France did not have such significant and deep-seated interests in the Americas at that time, and they were geographically separated by vast oceans, the means of transportation and technology were not as advanced as they are today. Therefore, the Americans were allowed to sing "America for Americans" and effectively control the politics and economy of two continents with one country. But in fact, the United States has had to abandon the Monroe Doctrine policy. Now, if Japan sings the Asian Monroe Doctrine to facilitate control of China, then before China is detached from its semi-colonial status, the European and American countries have intricate and profound political and economic interests in China, and even have a profound impact militarily. If Japan now wants to exclude the nations, placing China under absolute control with the slogan of "East Asia for East Asians", not only will the United States and Russia be hostile to Japan, but all European countries will be hostile to Japan, especially conflicting with British interests. The United States' control of the Americas was achieved after the American Revolutionary War and the acquisition of the dominant position. Japan's strength is the result of British conservation. This is something that the Japanese and the British cannot forget. Now, if Japan blatantly disregards this and considers itself the master of East Asia, the result will not only be that the whole world will be Japan's enemy.

(3) The Error of Self-Created Illusions: In order to encourage and spur on its people and unify domestic public opinion, Japan has previously pointed to Manchuria as Japan's lifeline for various exaggerated and untrue reasons. After the September 18th Incident, it further argued that its invasion of China was unavoidable because Japan's survival was threatened. At the same time, it frantically shouted to the Japanese people about its unprecedented national crisis, without considering that this kind of national crisis, even if it existed, was created by Japan itself. If it wanted to resolve it, it would be as easy as turning its mind around. Japan often accuses China of implementing anti-Japanese education. In fact, apart from narrating the history of national humiliation, China has not had any profound anti-Japanese education. Japan, on the other hand, has created illusions and instilled a deep-seated anti-Chinese mentality in its people, almost injecting the mentality of "either China or Japan" into the minds of every Japanese youth and child. This kind of creation of common and deep illusions to facilitate temporary national policies will have extremely serious consequences. From the facts, if Japan truly cares about its survival and development, the current approach can be said to be counterproductive. Because if Japan cannot completely eliminate China and leave no one alive, today's blatant disregard will never be like the destruction of Korea under the dynasty. It has been thirty years since Korea fell, but the Korean people today cannot be said to truly belong to Japan. Now, if it invades China to the end, permanently occupies Manchuria, or expands its scope further, and on the other hand uses piecemeal control methods to put China to death, then the Chinese people will not forget it even after three hundred years, let alone thirty years. This is a deep hatred that will last for generations in the closely adjacent China, and this is the threat to Japan's long-term survival. On the other hand, if Japan truly has the sincerity to automatically renew its national relations, then the difficult problems of the survival of the Japanese people can easily be solved by resolving Sino-Japanese pending issues, establishing Sino-Japanese relations, and seeking extremely reasonable solutions for maintaining peace in the Orient. China and Japan are geographically and ethnically close, and their customs and habits are also slightly similar. Just looking at the happy family relationships of those who marry between the two countries and the close and harmonious interactions between ordinary Chinese and Japanese businessmen, it can be seen that they are brothers and there is no reason why they cannot cooperate. The good example of self-strengthening and self-reliance in the Japanese Meiji Restoration gave the awakened Chinese people a lot of encouragement. China does not deny Japan's advanced achievements in academia, culture, industry, and economy. China is now in a period of revival and nation-building and urgently needs economic and cultural support. The Japanese people's hardworking and frugal habits are also suitable for cooperation with China. What Japan lacks may be seen as surplus in China. Conversely, what Japan can supply may be what China needs. Therefore, economically speaking, if the two countries can truly support each other on an equal and mutually beneficial basis, the problems of the survival and development of the two peoples can be completely solved.

Thinking calmly, there is really no need to restrict and restrain each other to move towards extinction together. (To be continued)

Rice Industry Market Ended Yesterday, Stopped Measuring by Dou 109

The Miscellaneous Grains Association Announced That Traders Should Pay Attention to Foreign Rice

The Total Amount of Rice Stored in Shanghai is Estimated to be More Than One Million Shi

Da Gong Society reports: The Shanghai Miscellaneous Grains Industry Association announced yesterday that various traders should pay attention to ordering foreign rice. The rice industry market in the north and south of the city ended yesterday. The total amount of rice stored in Shanghai is estimated to be more than one million shi. The details are as follows:

Announcement to Traders to Pay Attention to Foreign Rice: The Miscellaneous Grains Association issued Announcement No. 2 on the market yesterday, stating: "Last summer, there was a severe drought that caused a disaster, and the autumn harvest was poor. In order to prevent public panic over food, ordering foreign rice to provide supplies is a vital plan. However, the association recently investigated the amount of foreign rice ordered from various foreign firms. In Shanghai, 150,400 tons have arrived, 53,700 tons are en route, and 345,300 tons have been confirmed but not yet shipped. The total amount reaches 549,400 tons. In addition, 125,200 tons have been purchased in Ningbo. The total of the two places is 674,600 tons. It was found that in the autumn of the 19th year of the Republic of China, the country was hit by a disaster and the amount of foreign rice ordered was only 7-8 million bags. Last year's disaster was not as severe as in the past, but the amount of foreign rice purchased is so large. The association believes that it is necessary to pay attention. The association will hereby disclose a list of the amount of foreign rice confirmed by various foreign firms recently. It is hoped that all traders will pay attention. This is hereby announced on January 28th of the 24th year of the Republic of China."

Rice Industry Market Ended Yesterday: The rice industry market on Minguo Road in this city ended yesterday. All deliveries have been stopped. Traders are handling year-end closing procedures. The various river-bottom rice boats in the north and south districts will stop measuring by dou today. After the boatmen settle their accounts, they will return home to celebrate the New Year in the next few days. The market is scheduled to open and resume measuring by dou on February 8th of the Gregorian calendar.

Survey of the Total Amount of Rice Stored in Shanghai: During the Lunar New Year, rice prices are still trending stable. The highest price for white rice is 13.3 yuan and the lowest is 10 yuan. The highest price for Ke Xian rice is 11.4 yuan and the lowest is 9.12 yuan. The highest price for foreign rice is 11 yuan and the lowest is 10.07 yuan. Regarding the total amount of rice stored in this city, a reporter from Da Gong Society investigated yesterday that: (1) The reserve of river-bottom white rice is 100,000 shi in the south city and 150,000 shi in the north city. (2) Hunan Hankou Shashi Wuhu, etc. Ke Xian rice 176,664 bags. (5) Saigon No. 1, No. 2, No. 3, Siamese machine rice, and broken rice 500,600 bags.

Mr. Haas is scheduled to visit Mr. Song first after arriving in Shanghai, then go to Beijing, and then travel to various provinces for inspection. He is scheduled to stay in China for three months. Mr. Haas is French and previously came to China with the Lytton Survey Team as its Secretary-General.

The Safety Issue of Transporting Antiquities to England for Exhibition is Resolved 112

A Preview Exhibition Will Be Held in Shanghai Starting on the 15th of Next Month

An Antiquities Storage in Nanjing will be Completed Next Spring

The International Exhibition of Chinese Art is scheduled to open in England in November of this year. To ensure the matter is handled with the utmost care, the government has specially ordered the establishment of a Preparatory Committee to oversee it. It was also decided that a preview exhibition would be held in Shanghai three months before the antiquities are shipped, and another exhibition would be held in Shanghai when the antiquities are returned to China next year before being transported to Nanjing for storage. Details are as follows:

Safety Concerns The Chinese Art Exhibition is being held in England this year. This initiative was proposed by the British and only became a reality with the agreement of our government. However, the academic communities in both the North and South of China attach great importance to the transportation of these antiquities to England. They have also issued opinions and suggestions to the government, urging careful handling to prevent any loss of these cultural treasures and historical relics. In response, the government has specifically instructed the London Chinese Art Exhibition Committee to thoroughly investigate the safety measures for transporting the antiquities to England and submit a report for approval. The Preparatory Committee held its fourth meeting in Nanjing yesterday, where decisions were made regarding the procedures for packing and shipping the antiquities, as well as safety during transportation and exhibition. The British side will be fully responsible for everything after the antiquities leave the country. All plans will be communicated to the British side through our embassy in England by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs.

Preparing for the Preview Exhibition Regarding the preview exhibition to be held in Shanghai within three months, the Preparatory Committee has specifically invited several members from Shanghai and requested Mayor Wu's assistance and guidance. Pan Gongzhan will serve as the honorary secretary in Shanghai. After Pan located the old site of the Bank of China for rental, he immediately consulted with the Preparatory Committee in Nanjing via long-distance telephone and reached an agreement. Starting from the 15th of this month, personnel will be dispatched to arrange the exhibition site, which includes the first, second, and third floors. As for the selection of antiquities, the Preparatory Committee will send special committee member and Secretary-General Yang Zhensheng to Shanghai next month to select items from the Palace Museum warehouse with Chairman Wang Yunwu and others.

Construction of the Storage Facility Separately, according to antiquities inventory specialist Shu Chushi, speaking to a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency, the antiquities will be transported to Nanjing for storage after the exhibition in England next year. The construction of the antiquities storage facility in Nanjing has been decided to take place at the Chaotian Palace in Nanjing. The construction budget has been set at 600,000 yuan. It is learned that the government has already allocated 200,000 yuan to start construction, which is expected to be completed next spring. Once the inventory of the antiquities stored in Shanghai is completed, they will all be transported to Nanjing for storage.

Results of Physical Examinations of School-Age Children by the Anti-Tuberculosis Association 118

Younger Children are Physically Healthier

Adults in the North are Physically Stronger than Those in the South

China has long been known as the "Sick Man of East Asia," and the number of people suffering from lung diseases is especially high. Local medical experts, aware of this, have initiated the organization of the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association. A reporter from Guomin News visited Mr. Zhang Junjun, the executive director of the Association, yesterday to inquire about the results of the Association's school-age children's disease seedling tests, which are recorded as follows:

Tuberculosis Seedling Tests Reveal Weak Children According to Mr. Zhang, a total of 385 school-age children were tested this time. Medical officers from the Association's First Tuberculosis Clinic conducted the tests. The results of the tests are as follows: Among the 3 tested under the age of 5, one had a positive reaction and two had negative reactions. The positive reaction rate was 33.30%. Among the 180 children aged 6 to 10, 98 had positive reactions and 82 had negative reactions. The positive reaction rate was 54.40%. Among the 194 children aged 11 to 15, 52 had positive reactions and 42 had negative reactions. The positive reaction rate was 60.35%. Among the 5 individuals over the age of 16, four had positive reactions and one had a negative reaction. The positive reaction rate was 80.00%.

Northerners are Healthier, Southerners are Weaker According to Mr. Zhang, tuberculosis is not hereditary. Judging from this test, it is known that the phenomenon of increased response to germ tests in school-age children increases with age. After testing Chinese people over the age of 20, those with positive reactions account for as much as 98%. The weakness of the Chinese people's physique is evident from this. For example, last year, the Ministry of Education inspected the development of college students nationwide. Among 1,632 students at Peking University, 109 were classified as first-class development. Among 1,608 students at Sichuan University, only 499 were classified as first-class development. Among 1,285 students at Central University, only 278 were classified as first-class development. Furthermore, Kong Ershi of Peking University conducted 2,049 tuberculosis seedling tests, and the results showed that 231 had positive reactions, accounting for 30%. Lai of Shanghai Medical College conducted 4,703 tuberculosis seedling tests, and the results showed that 2,821 had positive reactions, accounting for 60%. From this, it can be seen that the percentage of southern students infected with tuberculosis germs is 60%, while the percentage of northern students is only 30%. Southerners are physically weaker than Northerners. Mr. Zhang also said that the proportion of Chinese people suffering from lung diseases is 4%, while in the United States, only 78 out of 100,000 people have lung diseases.

Report on Huai'ning Relief Efforts by the Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee 120

The drought was quite severe in Anhui Province. Gentry and merchants from Anqing, along with foreigners residing in the area, organized a temporary relief association and sent representatives to Shanghai to solicit aid, pleading with tears in their eyes. The Chinese and Foreign Famine Relief Committee allocated 3,000 yuan, and the Jisheng Society contributed 2,000 yuan, totaling 5,000 yuan for relief. According to the letter received, an investigation was conducted in the most severely affected areas of Huaining: Zongpu, Yanshan, Guanyinbao, Wayaoyin, Shaqiao, Hengshanyan, Wuxianmiao, Nuanshuisi, Hongmiao, Lingquan, and Shibaoli. The neediest drought victims, including the elderly and young children, were identified, limited to 1,000 people. Each person was to receive 5 yuan in relief, distributed over four months: 2 yuan in the first month and 1 yuan in each of the following three months. However, the investigation teams witnessed truly tragic situations in various districts. The current relief funds are meager, like a drop in the bucket, insufficient to sustain them. They urgently hope for more fundraising efforts. A report on the conditions of drought victims in the countryside is summarized below. According to the provincial government's on-site investigation of the drought in Anhui Province last year, 49 out of 60 counties were affected. The affected farmland totaled 18,161,426 mu, and the loss of rice was estimated at 50,489,356 shi, with a value loss of over 280 million yuan. The drought-affected population was estimated at 8,718,540 people. Elders say that even the great drought of the sixth year of the Xianfeng reign during the Qing dynasty was not as severe as this; it is truly a rare and unprecedented disaster. As the harsh winter approaches, the livelihoods of the drought victims are even more dire and in imminent danger. Therefore, provincial authorities initiated a winter relief fundraising campaign, calling upon various groups and charities to contribute enthusiastically. The Tianzhutang South Association in the city, deeply concerned about the plight of the refugees, dispatched He Xuren, Liu Hengwang, and Fei Wenbin on January 10th to distribute relief tickets and clothing to Guanyinbao, Wayao, Hengshan, Wuxian, Hongmiao, Lingquan, and other places. Although the work is now complete, we feel compelled to write this report to inform the readers of the suffering of the drought victims. The third to seventh districts of Huaining County are mostly hilly and prone to drought. Unexpectedly, last year's drought caused enormous losses, with an estimated 264,760 mu of farmland affected and 402,530 people suffering. The loss of rice, beans, wheat, and other crops amounted to 661,800 shi. In all the places we visited, the fields were barren, and the livelihoods of farmers were on the verge of collapse. Beggars selling their children and wives were a common sight by the roadside. The most tragic situations were in Lingquan and other places bordering Huaining and Wangjiang. Nine out of ten farmers had nothing left. The draft animals died. The elderly and weak awaited death, and the strong fled. The daily life of residents mainly consisted of filling their stomachs with radishes and daylily. The most impoverished boiled and ate sweet potato leaves, fertilizer grass, malt, duckweed, and manicao grass. Some even dried and ground coarse bran, oil tree bark, and flaxseed roots to make porridge. There were even those who ate Guanyin clay and committed suicide by taking poison or hanging themselves. The drought victims lived crammed together in one bed with several family members, with only a bundle of straw and tattered cotton wadding for bedding. The suffering caused by the severe cold is unimaginable. If the authorities delay in providing adequate assistance, the drought victims will be left to die.

The Red Swastika Society Welcomes Chairman Xiong Shihui 121

The three chairmen of the Red Swastika Society, Xiong Xiling, Zhang Lanping, and Han Shichang, held a tea party at their office in the Zhonghe Village on Bubbling Well Road on the afternoon of the 27th to welcome Xiong Shihui, Chairman of the Jiangxi Provincial Government. Attendees included Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Huang Hanzhi, Zhu Qinglan, Guan Gangzhi, Huang Bodu, and over fifty key staff members of the society. The government has separately handled relief, burial, medical care, and rural construction. However, Jiangxi's finances are exhausted after the great chaos, and it is difficult to balance everything. He hopes that all sectors of society will provide assistance with the same spirit and determination as the society, so that the tens of millions of drought victims in Jiangxi can all be relieved. He bowed deeply to plead for the disaster victims. The guests and hosts parted on amicable terms after 5 o'clock.

Bank of China Relocates and Forms Old Building Management Committee 123

Construction Plans Still Undecided

The Bank of China, formerly located at 22 The Bund, planned to relocate due to the age of the building and rebuild it. They selected the building at 50 Hankou Road, but the ongoing road elevation project at that location caused transportation inconvenience, delaying the move until yesterday. A Central News Agency reporter visited the new bank premises yesterday and spoke with the head of the General Affairs Department, learning the details of the relocation as follows:

Relocation in Stages　Due to the large number of departments in the bank, simultaneous relocation would be difficult. Therefore, it was carried out in two stages. The first stage, involving the General Management Department, was completed yesterday (the 28th). Other departments, such as the Foreign Exchange Department, the Shanghai Branch, and the Trust Department, continue to operate at the original location. They will be relocated during the three-day lunar New Year holiday on February 5th, 6th, and 7th, and will resume normal operations at the new location from February 8th.

Allocation of New Building　The new building has four floors, and the allocation of office space is as follows: (Ground Floor) Business Hall, Foreign Exchange Department, Trust Department, Manager's Office, Deputy Manager's Office; (First Floor) Insurance Company, Shanghai Branch Document Section, Regional Branch, Securities Department, Securities Department Custody Section, Inspection Committee; (Second Floor) Board of Directors Office, General Manager's Office, General Secretary's Office, Chief Auditor's Office, Personnel Office, General Affairs Department, Business Investigation Department, Inspection Office, Business Management Office First Section, Business Management Second Section, Business Management Third Section; (Third Floor) General Ledger Room, Economic Research Office, Stock Affairs Office, Building Department Supervisor's Office, General Affairs Department Materials Section Dining Hall.

Management of Old Building　Regarding the old building at 22 The Bund, the bank has appointed seven members from various departments to form the Old Building Management Committee. The committee will decide on matters such as demolition, design, and bidding for the old building. It is said that after the bank has completely moved out, a certain organization intends to borrow the premises for an exhibition, but only for a short period. As for how to rebuild, how many floors to build, when to demolish, and when to construct, nothing has been decided yet, as the Public Works Department will impose various restrictions on the construction of the new building, such as the number of floors and land concessions, and negotiations will take time.

Grand Opening of the Guangdong Bank's New Building 124

Located at 52 Ningbo Road, at the intersection of Jiangxi Road, Shanghai, the new building of the Guangdong Bank has been completed. The grand opening ceremony will be held this morning. At that time, the bank's entrance will surely be bustling with activity, reaching its peak. The bank has a history of over 30 years, established in the early years of the Republic of China. Five years after the establishment of the Hong Kong headquarters, a branch was set up in Shanghai. The capital has increased from 2 million Hong Kong dollars to over 11 million Hong Kong dollars. Since its establishment in Shanghai, the bank has held the economic pivot between China and foreign countries in both Hong Kong and Shanghai. Foreign merchants used to handle the exchange of various currencies in China, but the bank has been engaged in foreign exchange business with painstaking effort, gradually competing with foreign banks. The Number of Poor People Seeking Shelter at the Charity Shelter Increases Dramatically in the Cold Winter 126

Since its opening, the number of poor people seeking shelter at the Shanghai South Charity Shelter has been increasing daily. The Chaohui Villa and Chaozhou Guild Hall have already accommodated over 2,700 people. Donations of funds, clothing, and bedding from various sectors have been very enthusiastic in recent days, as detailed in various newspapers. Yesterday (the 27th), the First Women's Wounded Soldier Hospital in the city donated all 265 of its stored blankets to the Shanghai Charity Organizations Joint Association at the Renji Charity Hall on Six Ma Road for distribution to the shelter for relief. However, since the snowfall the day before yesterday, the number of poor people seeking shelter has increased dramatically, leading to severe overcrowding. Therefore, there may not be enough clothing and bedding. It is hoped that philanthropists from all walks of life will donate generously to help the poor and the needy get through the end of the year, which would be a truly immeasurable act of merit.

Two Railways to Organize Plum Blossom Viewing Tours 127

From February 9th to March 24th

Enjoy Plum Blossoms in Hangzhou, Linping, and Wuxi

The plum blossoms in Hangzhou, Linping, and Wuxi are all famous and have their own characteristics. In Hangzhou, in addition to the plum blossoms planted by the recluse Lin Bu's wife on Gushan Mountain, there are the five-colored plum blossoms of Lingfeng. Linping has the ancient Song plum blossoms of Luying. As for the plum blossoms of the Meiyuan Garden in Wuxi, they are especially known for their abundant branches and lush clusters, and have long been widely praised. The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, considering that the plum blossoms in various places along the railway line are about to bloom, and those who wish to visit and admire them will surely be enthusiastic, have prepared plum blossom viewing tours on both lines. The plum blossom viewing period will be from February 9th to March 24th, with Hangzhou, Linping, and Wuxi as the destinations. During this period, it is said that the railway administration will assign staff at each station to guide tourists and provide various conveniences to plum blossom viewing travelers. In addition, a plum blossom photography competition will be held simultaneously, and prizes will be awarded to the winners to increase interest and leave memories. The Traffic Department of the administration is currently compiling a plum blossom viewing publication with very detailed content, which will be distributed to various sectors. It is expected that the publication will be released in about ten days.

Minutes of the Shareholders' Meeting of the Grain Exchange 128

The Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Cake Exchange held its 18th annual shareholders' meeting at its location on Aidoa Road on the afternoon of the 27th at 3:00 PM. Over fifty people, including Gu Xinyi, attended. The meeting was chaired by Chairman Gu Xinyi, and important proposals were discussed. The following is a summary: (1) The rental arrears for the property on Minkuo Road, due up to the end of March 1934, amounted to 5,219.83 yuan. After deducting the 2,400 yuan received, 2,819.83 yuan remains outstanding. The board of directors should be urged to collect the arrears promptly. (2) Since the Exchange took over the collection of rent for the property on Minkuo Road, Dongming and Tongxing still owe rent. Although there are methods, they must be collected urgently. In addition to the existing lease agreements and rent books, the board of directors should handle the matter in accordance with the City Police Bureau's rent collection regulations. (3) Regarding the mortgage on the Taishan Wheel, as the wheel has now sunk, how should it be dealt with? Please have the board of directors handle it. (4) The long-term debt of Hua Da handled by the Exchange Federation has not been repaid with interest for two years. Please have the board of directors urge its collection. (5) Regarding the large sum of over 15,000 yuan previously owed in the name of Broker No. 14, are the repayment procedures legal? Please have the board of directors provide a clear explanation.

Tianjin Icebound, Shipping Companies to Raise Freight Rates by 20% 129

The weather in North China is colder, and Tianjin is already icebound. Merchant ships traveling from Tanggu Port to Baihe River are now using icebreakers for navigation. It is more difficult for Shanghai's Northern Ocean liners to navigate the Baihe River upon arrival in Tianjin. The local shipping companies decided yesterday after public discussion that from February 1st, i.e., Friday, all goods shipped from Shanghai to Tianjin will be subject to an icebound fee, which will be an additional 20% of the original freight rate. All companies have already notified the customs brokers and shippers to take note of this.

Truck Driver Who Ran Over and Killed a Person Interrogated in Court 130

Ling Zhixiang, a rickshaw puller from Taixing, residing at No. 8 Renshou Lane, Lane 125, Caishi Road, French Concession, is 34 years old this year. He lives alone in Shanghai pulling a rickshaw. At 2:30 PM on the 27th, Ling was pulling his rickshaw on Rue Paul Beau, French Concession, heading east. At No. 76 on that road, a garbage truck No. 717 of the French Public Works Department, driven by Xu Lianhai, from Jiangbei, was traveling in the same direction from behind. Due to the driver's negligence, Ling was knocked down, and the rear wheel of the truck ran over Ling's lower body, causing his leg bones to be broken. The police officer saw this and sent the injured person to Guangci Hospital. Due to the severity of his injuries, he died four hours later. The police sent the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch for examination. Yesterday, Prosecutor Wang of the Second Special Court, accompanied by a forensic doctor and a clerk, arrived at the scene to verify that the deceased died from being run over by a car before his death. As the matter pertained to his home village, and he had no relatives in Shanghai, the car owner, Wang Yanzhi, came forward to request to claim the body for burial. After the official interrogated the defendant about the circumstances of the accident, he approved Wang Yanzhi's request to claim the body for burial. The defendant was sent to the hospital for questioning by the police department. It is said that the police will send the defendant to court today for interrogation. Regarding the damages to the deceased, the defendant has asked someone to contact the car owner to discuss compensation with the deceased's family.

Municipal Ferry Double-Decker Pier Opens 131

Floating Restaurant to Open Soon

The Shanghai Industrial and Trust Company's double-decker pier, located on the Bund near Beijing Road, has opened yesterday. The floating restaurant is in the planning and arrangement stage. The details are as follows:

Double-Decker Pier Opened Yesterday　For the purpose of developing the ferry business, the Shanghai Industrial and Trust Company built a double-decker steel-framed pier on the Bund near Beijing Road, at the Municipal Council Pier. The construction was completed on the 12th of this month, but it was repeatedly postponed due to the widening of the original pedestrian walkway. It finally opened yesterday. The pier has a novel and solid structure and a magnificent appearance. The entire building has two floors. The upper floor houses the management office and passenger waiting room, and the lower floor houses the ticket office, small shops, and a passenger waiting room, so that passengers can rest before boarding or after disembarking. The south end of the pier is the entrance for pedestrians, and the north end is the exit for pedestrians. All long-distance ferries to Gaoqiao and Wusong, as well as short-distance ferries to Pudong across the river, docked at the new pier starting yesterday morning. The ferries across the river start at 5:00 AM daily, and the long-distance ferries start at 8:00 AM. The old municipal ferry pier on the Bund near Nanjing Road has been closed.

Floating Restaurant to Open Soon　No ceremony was held when the new pier opened yesterday.

Tan Boying, the manager of the company, along with Assistant Manager An, were stationed at the pier all day yesterday, overseeing and arranging everything, and were quite busy. The first docking of the long-distance and short-distance ferries was met with crowded passengers. In order to provide passengers with a comfortable place to rest, the company plans to open a floating restaurant in the remaining space on the upper floor of the pier. However, due to the time required for various arrangements, it is expected that the restaurant will officially open soon. In the future, the restaurant will have all the necessary internal facilities, making it a unique place to relax on the water.

Shanghai East China Products Exhibition Closed Yesterday 132
