Jicheng Pharmacy Resumed Business Yesterday 133

Debts to Be Repaid in Installments Starting June 30th

Actively Pursuing Collection of Debts and Developing Business

Jicheng Pharmacy on Nanjing Road, Shanghai, formerly known as Jicheng Gongji Pharmacy, was forced to temporarily suspend business on the 28th of last month due to the sluggish market, the accumulation of inventory, and the withdrawal of deposits by depositors, which made it impossible to cope with. It is now known that the company, after a shareholders' meeting on the 27th, decided to resume business immediately, as more than three-quarters of the creditors had agreed to and signed the reconciliation plan. It officially resumed business at 9:00 AM yesterday. The details learned by the New News Agency reporter are as follows:

Shareholders' Meeting Decides to Resume Business　After Jicheng Gongji Pharmacy declared a temporary suspension of business, it held a shareholders' meeting on the 12th of this month and decided on two methods for resuming business. If the consent of more than three-quarters of the creditors was obtained by the 25th of this month, it would resume business immediately; otherwise, it would be liquidated. After the notice of the reconciliation and resumption plan was sent to each creditor, the creditors made some modifications to it. As of the 25th of this month, creditors with a total of over 310,900 yuan had signed their agreement, which accounted for more than three-quarters of the total debt of over 414,000 yuan. Therefore, the company held a shareholders' meeting at its original location on Nanjing Road on the afternoon of the 27th and decided (1) that the company should resume business immediately, (2) that a shareholders' meeting should be convened at 2:00 PM on February 17th, (3) that it should immediately apply to the court for record-keeping, and (4) that it should notify the lawyers and accountants to finalize the reconciliation case. Therefore, it officially started business at 9:00 AM yesterday.

Collecting Debts and Reorganizing Business　The New News Agency reporter visited the company yesterday morning and was received by Mr. Shen, who said that the company was fortunate to have the understanding and mutual benefit of all the creditors, who signed their agreement to the company's reconciliation plan, which enabled it to resume business today. However, after the suspension of business, there was a lot of internal backlog that needed to be reorganized. In addition, the Lunar New Year was approaching, and if the debts were not collected quickly, there would be no time to do so. The company has a total of over 160,000 yuan in outstanding debts, which need to be actively collected to serve as working capital. As for the purchase of goods, the industry is very concerned about the company and is willing to maintain it. Therefore, after the resumption of business, there are no problems with the future of the business.

Creditor Reconciliation Plan　Reconciliation Plan between Jicheng Gongji Pharmacy Co., Ltd. and Creditors: (1) The debt of Jicheng Gongji Pharmacy Co., Ltd. will be repaid in equal installments over ten years, starting from June 30th of this year. The first repayment will be on June 30th, 1935, and repayments will be made successively every year on June 30th. If the company has a surplus at the end of each year, the company will pay interest at a weekly rate of 4%, and the interest will decrease with the principal. (2) If the company still has a surplus after repaying the principal and interest each year, the company should repay the principal of the debt in advance in equal installments. (3) If the company only repays the principal of the debt within ten years and has no surplus to pay interest, the unpaid interest will only be paid from the company's surplus after the principal has been repaid, but compound interest will not be calculated. (4) After the company resumes business, it shall not withdraw shareholder official profits, bonuses, and transportation expenses from the surplus each year before the principal and interest of the debt have been repaid. (5) If the amount of debt is less than 100 yuan, it is not subject to the above reconciliation plan. The above reconciliation plan should be approved by the shareholders' meeting at the request of the board of directors. (6) The creditors agree to the above reconciliation plan and hereby sign and affix their seals below. (Omitted)

Yong'an Silver Company Sued Again by Creditors 134

Company Seeks Second Resumption of Business

Lin Kanghou Denies Being a Director

Yong'an Silver Company on North Sichuan Road, which opened in September of last year, only operated for three months before suddenly suspending business in December. Later, General Manager Ou Jiancheng left Shanghai to find a solution and hired Sun Zufu as the new manager, and the company recently began to resume business. However, within a few days, it was stranded again. Because the company did not have a concrete plan for the deposits of general depositors, Wang Weiguan, manager of Delong Tobacco Company, sued the company's chairman, Deng Jinghuan, and others for fraud for failing to pay the deposits of 50,000 yuan. The First Special Court has held several hearings, but has not yet concluded the case. Now, depositors Gu Zhenji, Zhang Yinji, Guangxinghao, and other 30 creditors, with an estimated 10,000 yuan in fixed-term and current deposits, have elected Peng Zican, Zhu Wenkui, Yao Keming, Zhang Yinji, and other four persons as representatives, and hired lawyer Zhang Qingyue to sue the Yong'an Silver Company's chairman Deng Jinghuan, vice chairman Wang Jiazhen, directors Mo Dehui, Lin Kanghou, Zhang Zilian, Ye Hancheng, Lin Qiuhu, Qian Youju, Peng Baohui, Jiang Qi, Gu Chuntao, director and general manager Ou Jiancheng, and manager Dai Kechang, and 13 others for fraud and obtaining property, requesting that they be summoned and interrogated according to law. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Judge Wu Zehan held a hearing in the Second Criminal Court. The summonses for the defendants were all collected by lawyer Jiang Yiping, but none of them appeared in court. Only Ou Jiancheng retained lawyer Li Shirui to appear in court, stating that some of the defendants were in Peiping, and that the summonses for the remaining defendants had just been delivered to lawyer Jiang last night, so they could not be forwarded in time, and requested a postponement. Judge Wu then asked lawyer Li about the internal organization and total capital of Yong'an Silver Company. Lawyer Li replied that the company's total capital was said to be 1 million yuan, and that it was registered in the United States for the convenience of international transactions. The defendants in this case are all directors, and the shareholders have subscribed for shares, with each share being 100 yuan, for a total subscription of more than 500,000 yuan, but only more than 200,000 yuan was actually paid up, and some shareholders have paid up, while others have not. Chairman Deng Jinghuan subscribed for 20,000 yuan in shares, and the company began operations in September. In December, due to the impact of the collapse of Jiande Bank, six 10,000 yuan promissory notes could not be collected, resulting in a temporary financial crisis and a declaration of suspension of business. The total amount owed is about 220,000 yuan, and the amount owed to the company is 180,000 yuan. Of this amount, the 60,000 yuan owed by Jiande Bank is not easy to collect, but the remaining 120,000 yuan can be recovered gradually. After making every effort to find a solution and hiring Sun Zufu as the manager, the company began to resume business. During this period of resumption, the depositors have successively withdrawn 60,000 to 70,000 yuan of deposits, only because Manager Sun allowed a 65,000 yuan advance at the time, but the result was that not a single cent was received. Recently, Sun signed a statement at lawyer Jiang Yiping's office, willing to find a way to pay 40,000 yuan first, but it did not materialize, so the business was suspended again. The situation is critical at the moment, and efforts are being made to find a way to resume business. Therefore, the creditor in the other case, Delong Tobacco Company, has also understood and has already repaid part of the deposit, 17,000 yuan, and the remaining amount will be repaid at 5,000 yuan per month, and a settlement should be reached. Lawyer Zhang, the agent of the plaintiff, stated that he represented 30 creditors, with about 7 households of fixed-term deposits amounting to more than 6,000 yuan, and the remaining 20 households, all current accounts and transactions, amounting to more than 3,000 yuan. In addition to submitting the deposit slips for each debt, he also presented two pieces of evidence: one is a letter from Lin Kanghou denying that he is a director of the company, and the other is a directive from the Social Bureau to all newspapers to stop publishing the company's advertisements because the company suddenly announced its suspension of business and then resumed business, which was obviously inappropriate. Finally, lawyer Li, the agent of the defendant, stated that Lin Kanghou was indeed a director, and that the company was scheduled to resume business, at the latest around the eighth day of the Lunar New Year, so he requested a postponement. Judge Wu then ordered the case to be adjourned to February 13th at 2:00 PM for further hearing. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Rickshaw Pullers Who Picked Up a Diamond Ring and Pawned It for Profit Fined 135

Two Pawnbroker Owners Acquitted

Lu Ada and Lu Asan, rickshaw pullers from Chongming, previously picked up a diamond gold ring lost by a Mr. Feng in Fuyu Lane. Because they could not tell if it was real or fake, they took it to Hongxing Pawnshop on North Sichuan Road for appraisal. A strangely dressed man wanted to buy it, but the price could not be agreed upon, so they gave up. A few days later, the man rented a room in a hotel and invited the two Lus to go there. He gave them 900 yuan to buy the diamond ring. Later, the police learned of this and arrested the Lus for concealing the found property, secretly selling it, and profiting from it, which was illegal. Wu Shangshou and Wu Shanglu, the owners of Hongxing Pawnshop, were also suspected of receiving stolen goods and were sued in the same case. After repeated hearings by Judge Ye Shengchao of the First Special District Court, the two Wus hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to defend them, and presented accounting books to prove the legality of their business. Judge Ye himself went to the pawnshop and its affiliate, Hong Kong Jewelry Company, for detailed inspection. Yesterday morning, the court announced the judgment in the case. Lu Ada was fined 140 yuan, and Lu Asan was fined 110 yuan. If they were unable to pay, they would be imprisoned for one day for every two yuan. Wu Shangshou and Wu Shanglu were acquitted. During the appeal period, they were all allowed to remain released on bail.

Pawnshop Accountant Embezzles Funds and Escapes to Guangdong by Plane 136

Valuable Ornaments Pledged

Clerk Suspected of Conspiracy

Zhang Junyi, from Guangdong, independently opened Baoxing Pawnshop at No. 547 Avenue Joffre, French Concession. His younger brother, Zhang Jinxing, served as the accountant, and Zhang Rusheng was hired as the clerk. On the 21st of this month, Zhang Jinxing ordered Zhang Rusheng to pledge valuable ornaments such as diamonds, jewelry, and jade, worth more than 10,000 yuan, which had been pawned daily in the store, to another pawnshop. At the time, Rusheng refused. Jinxing said that the store's cash flow was tight and he had no choice but to pledge them. Rusheng still refused. Jinxing then said, "The store is owned by my brothers, and we have not divided the property. If there is any dispute in the future, I will be responsible for it alone. If you don't believe me, I can issue a written statement," not wanting to embarrass Rusheng. Rusheng then agreed and had Jinxing issue a written statement. He then took the ornaments to Yuchang Pawnshop and pledged them for 5,050 yuan. In front of the Pudong Bank on Sanmao Bridge, Aidoa Road, he handed over the money to Jinxing in full. Jinxing obtained the money and went to China Aviation Company on Five Ma Road to buy an air ticket from Shanghai to Guangdong and escaped to Guangdong by plane. When store owner Zhang Junyi discovered this, it was too late to pursue his brother, and he reported to the French Police that Zhang Rusheng was involved in conspiracy. The police sent detectives to arrest Zhang Rusheng the day before yesterday. Yesterday, he was sent to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special Court. Judge Li Changnian interrogated him. Police lawyer Fei Xizhen stated the case, saying that the police had not yet investigated the defendant's embezzlement in the course of business, and requested a postponement pending investigation. After questioning the defendant in court, the judge ordered a postponement to February 1st for further hearing. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Suspicious Assault Case 137

Mother Wounded by Knife, Son Afraid to Report to Police

Wang Xu, a 38-year-old widow from Hangzhou, lost her husband many years ago. She has a son named Wang Lijin, who is 17 years old. Due to the poverty of her family, the mother and son came to Shanghai to make a living. They rented a kitchen in Taide Lane, No. 10 Xujiahui Road, French Concession, and lived together. At around 4:00 PM on the 26th of this month, two unknown men suddenly broke into her bedroom and, without asking any questions, took out a sharp axe and slashed her head twice before leaving. She fell to the ground in pain and bleeding profusely. Her son was nearby at the time, but dared not make a sound. After the assailant fled, he hired a car to take her to the Southeast Hospital of the Shanghai Military Camp in the South City for treatment. After staying in the hospital for two days, her injuries worsened, and her son transferred her to Renji Hospital for treatment. The hospital reported the matter to the French Police as a murder case. The police sent detectives to investigate. As the case occurred in the French Concession, she was transferred to Guangci Hospital for treatment. At the same time, Kim Gu-lin, the inspector general of the Special Agency, dispatched his detectives to investigate the cause of the murder and arrest the assailant for interrogation. However, the reason is still under close investigation.

Female Tea Server Steals Female Customer's Watch 138

Sentenced to Thirty Days of Detention

Chen Suzhen, a 22-year-old woman from Hangzhou, residing at No. 372 Da Tong Road, works as a female tea server at the New-Shanghai Company rooftop garden playground. On the evening of the 25th of this month, at 7:10 PM, a Suzhou woman named Wen Lu (21 years old), residing at No. 49 Ruiji Lane, East Jiaxing Road, came to the garden to play. Due to a sudden urge, she went to the restroom. After finishing, she took off her fur coat and placed her wristwatch in the coat pocket, hanging it on the door. At that moment, Chen also went to the restroom, exiting before Wen. When Wen finished washing her hands, she discovered that her wristwatch was missing. At the time, only Chen Suzhen was in the restroom, and there was no one else. She searched everywhere for Chen without success. Therefore, on the 26th, she went to the garden again and confronted Chen, then turned her over to the Lao Zha police station for detention. Yesterday morning, she was escorted to the Second Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Police lawyer Zhang Shizhu prosecuted her for theft under Article 337 of the Criminal Law, based on Wen Lu's complaint.

Regarding the circumstances of the theft, Chen Suzhen claimed during interrogation that the wristwatch was found on the floor of the restroom and was not stolen. The court questioned her that if it was indeed found, she should have handed it over to the accounting office. Why did she take it home? She replied that she had not been working as a tea server for long and was unaware of the rules. Judge Ye Shengchao, based on the confession, sentenced Chen Suzhen to thirty days of detention in court as a warning.

Inauguration Ceremony of the General Headquarters of the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association Scheduled for February 6th 139

The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession, with the aim of improving the lives and treatment of rickshaw pullers, established the Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association. They invited enthusiastic members of society, including Li Denghui, Qiu Zitong, Xie Andao, Maxi, Yin Zhiling, Zhu Maocheng, and Wang Zhiren, as directors. Two locations, East Jiaxing Road and MacGen Road, were rented as temporary headquarters. The association was established in November of last year. Preliminary work, such as schools, clinics, bathhouses, teahouses, recreation rooms, reading rooms, etc., has been carried out in more than ten categories and has achieved considerable success, which is highly praised by society. It has recently been learned that the general headquarters of the association on East Jiaxing Road has been completed. Yesterday, the board of directors of the association decided to hold the inauguration ceremony on February 6th (i.e., the third day of the first lunar month). The general headquarters has a dormitory for rickshaw pullers, equipped with double-use iron beds, mattresses, sheets, quilts, storage boxes, etc. The accommodation fee is very low, calculated at six dimes per month, two dimes per week, or ten copper coins per day. It is also reported that the association has prepared invitations, inviting people from all walks of life to participate in the ceremony and provide guidance. Groups or individuals interested in social causes who have not received invitations are also very welcome to come and provide guidance.

Zhabei Charity Group Soup Kitchen Issues Rice Tickets Yesterday 141

The Liu Ying Road Second Soup Kitchen, organized by the Zhabei Charity Group, due to the surge in poor people drinking porridge, recently suddenly received a large number of Hubei refugees, about 400 people, totaling about 25,000 people in the entire factory, which was not enough to accommodate them. The bamboo fences and gates around the factory were completely collapsed, making it impossible to maintain order and fearing danger. It was suddenly announced the day before yesterday that the soup kitchen would be closed for the second time. The details have been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. The reporter of the Hua Dong News Agency yesterday specially visited Mr. Wang Binyan, the director of the group, to inquire about the follow-up measures. Mr. Wang said that the second closure of the Liu Ying Road Soup Kitchen was truly a last resort, and he felt extremely apologetic. The group has dispatched personnel from the day before yesterday to conduct surveys of the poor, and has now completed the task. Starting today, rice tickets will be distributed in different districts, totaling more than 400 dan. It is currently planned to expand the factory again on February 10th to increase its capacity and continue to open, to comfort the hungry people, and hoping that philanthropists will continue to provide relief.

China Land Reclamation Bank Relieves Rural Areas 142

Allocates Two Million Yuan for Pledged Agricultural Products

Establishes a Total of Nine Warehouses in This and Other Cities

The China Land Reclamation Bank has always been committed to supporting industry and commerce. It provides loans and makes every effort to support major domestic industries operated by Chinese people, such as cotton weaving, wool weaving, flour, electrical appliances, glass, and cement. Recently, in order to focus on rural revitalization, Chairman and General Manager Qin Runqing proposed at the meeting of the Standing Committee that the bank should increase the amount of loans with agricultural products as collateral within this year, aiming to reach two million yuan. On the one hand, it will increase the number of warehouses. In addition to the four warehouses already established in Shanghai, two in Tianjin, and one in Ningbo, it has recently established two cotton warehouses in Yangsi District, Pudong, with as many as fourteen warehouses in total. Currently, it has stored more than 20,000 bales of various seeds and cotton clothing, valued at more than one million yuan, which have been pledged to the bank. The lowest interest rate is only six and a half mills per month. At the same time, the bank has also seen that the construction of highways in the inland areas of Zhejiang has been progressing rapidly in recent years, and transportation has become increasingly convenient. It has decided to first select areas in Yin, Ci, and Yao to build rural warehouses and pledge various agricultural products at the lowest possible interest rates. In North China, the bank has undertaken a large amount of export discounting and loaning for products such as fur and cotton, providing unparalleled convenience to producers in terms of interest rates, exchange rates, and handling fees.

Postal Administration Announces the Cessation of Business for Private Letter Offices 143

Those Involved in Smuggling Will Be Prosecuted and Penalized According to Law

The private letter offices in this city have, after receiving orders from the Ministry of Communications to close, ceased operations one after another. All business licenses issued by the Postal Administration to these letter offices last year are naturally invalid. The post office hereby issues the following announcement: It is found that all private letter office businesses should cease operations in accordance with the Ministry's order from the first of this month. All business licenses issued last year have expired and should be invalidated. Hereafter, the public must deliver letters directly to the post office for delivery. Otherwise, if anyone dares to smuggle, they will be prosecuted and penalized according to law once apprehended. For fear of not being fully informed, this announcement is hereby issued.

General Election of the Chinese Islamic Association 144

The Shanghai Chinese Islamic Association on Qingyun Street has been established for many years and has achieved remarkable results, such as running the private Dunhua Elementary School, the Islamic Arabic Research Society, translating the Quran, and cultivating Islamic students to study abroad. The association is the only cultural institution in Shanghai's Islamic community. The general election of committee members was held the day before yesterday (27th). A total of 171 members attended the meeting. The Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters sent Mao Yun to the meeting to provide guidance. Representatives from various Islamic public organizations and mosques also attended the meeting. Sha Shanyu, Wu Yongxia, and Su Zixiang hosted the event. chairman, and Yang Jiashan as the recorder. First, Mr. Wu reported on the purpose of the meeting and the work done over the years. Then, Mr. Mao Yun delivered a speech on behalf of the Municipal Party Headquarters, with many words of encouragement. Due to the length of the speech, it cannot be recorded in detail. At 4:00 PM, members voted. As a result, Su Zixiang received 154 votes, Ma Jinqing 147 votes, Wu Yongxia 145 votes, Ha Dechen 138 votes, Sha Shanyu 124 votes, Shi Zifan 124 votes, Yang Jiashan 120 votes, Wu Tegong 108 votes, Li Yunsheng 92 votes, Da Pusheng 89 votes, Sun Yanwing 88 votes, Yang Shuping 87 votes, Jin Dunqing 76 votes, Ma Ziqing 72 votes, and Yang Gaozhi 68 votes, and were elected as executive members of the association. Five alternates were Fang Zijie, Ma Zhongnan, Sha Xiangzhi, Zong Ditang, and Jiang Su'an. The meeting adjourned when the lights were lit in every home.

Three Patients Fully Recovered and Discharged in One Day

In addition, Jin Aqiao, a female patient with epilepsy sent for treatment by the China Women and Children Relief Association, also fully recovered and was discharged yesterday. Her thank-you letter stated, "Respectfully, upon receiving a phone call informing us that Jin Aqiao, the woman sent by our association for medical treatment, has been cured, we are deeply grateful. We are sending someone to pick her up immediately. Please instruct the person to take her back, and we will find a way to repay the fees. Thank you in advance. Sincerely, China Women and Children Relief Association to China Mental Hospital."

Theft at the Zhang Family in Dachang Lane, Hugunying, Shanghai 149

A Large Amount of Gold Jewelry and Other Valuables

All Four Thieves Escaped Without a Trace

At around 9:00 AM yesterday morning, four robbers, dressed in different clothes and holding a pistol, broke into the home of Zhang Rongsheng, a Ningbo coppersmith residing at No. 24 Dachang Lane, Hugunying, Nanshi. Zhang Rongsheng happened to be out on business, and only Zhang's wife was in the living room. The robbers immediately pulled out their pistols and threatened everyone to keep silent. One robber monitored their actions, while the other three went to Zhang's bedroom on the front floor to search and rob. They stole three gold rings, one pearl ring, one gold-set gemstone ring, one gold bracelet, one pair each of pearl earrings and jade earrings, one satin fur coat, one flannel coat, and one camel wool coat, and one set of worsted gabardine jacket and pants. After the robbery, the four robbers put on the clothes and escaped with the stolen goods through the front door. Afterwards, Zhang Rongsheng reported the robbery to the Dongjiadu Police Station of the Public Security Bureau. After receiving the report, Chief Yi sent a patrol officer to investigate and reported the case to the headquarters for record. At the same time, he ordered the detectives stationed at the station to investigate and arrest the fleeing robbers and bring them to justice according to the law.

Tao Jishi Hangs Herself Due to Poverty 150

Tao Jishi, 26, the wife of Tao Chuande, a Haizhou native who worked as a coolie and lived in a straw shed at the northern end of Shixing Road, Zhabei, has always been on good terms with her husband. Recently, her husband fell ill and could not work, so he stayed at home to recuperate. She suddenly became alarmed about the problem of livelihood. Because Tao had only come to Shanghai recently and was unfamiliar with the area, she lacked assistance and was in a desperate situation. They faced each other in ragged clothes. Recently, her temperament changed drastically, and she kept writing in the air all day long, as if she had lost something. Her husband did not take it seriously. Unexpectedly, the night before last, she secretly hanged herself. Her husband was shocked when he realized it and tried to rescue her, but it was too late. The matter was discovered by the police station in charge. In addition to ordering the police to investigate the truth, they also ordered the local security officer Huang Hongsheng to go to the hospital to request an autopsy.

Liu Yinsheng, Who Took the Extortion Money from the Trash Can, Was Captured by Detectives 151

Yan Zaofang, a local resident, residing at No. 39 Deyuli, Dongyouheng Road, suddenly received a pair of anonymous threatening letters at around 8:00 PM on the 25th of this month, demanding 120 silver dollars. He was instructed to wrap the money in paper and put it in a trash can at the entrance at 9:00 PM the night before last. If someone came to take it, otherwise his life would be in danger. Yan immediately reported the information to the Jiaxing Road Police Station, which dispatched Chinese detective Xu Zhiqiong and detectives Lu Jinsheng and Lu Shouchang to wrap a hundred-dollar model in paper according to the letter, and added one silver dollar. They put it in the trash can at the appointed time and waited nearby. After a while, Liu Yinsheng, a Chongming native, 28 years old, arrived, opened the lid of the trash can, and took it out. Just as he was about to escape, he was arrested and taken to the police station. Yan identified him as a box maker working in the west wing of the same residence. The police chief ordered him to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Council lawyer Li Zhishan stated the previous situation and requested a postponement for further investigation of another case. Following the report of the Chinese and Western detectives detailing the events, the threatening letter was presented for inspection. The victim, Yan Zaofang, stated that he worked as a Chinese teacher at the Lao Zha police station. Unexpectedly, the defendant was a resident of the same place. When questioned, Liu Yinsheng confessed that the letter was written with a pencil in the nearby Xiaocai Market in an attempt to get lucky. He gave evasive answers and begged for leniency. Judge Xiao Yifen ordered him to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing.

Statistics of Books Borrowed from Shenbao Circulation Library Last Year 152

The Shenbao Circulation Library (3rd Floor, Continental Emporium, Nanjing Road) usually lends books at a fee, and has facilities for postal lending, reading, and reading guidance. The results are particularly good. Here are various statistics of the library for the 23rd year [of the Republic of China] as of the end of last year. The number of long-term readers with deposits has exceeded 10,000, and the current actual number of readers is more than 5,000. The age group of 16 to 25 years old is the largest, with more than 3,500 men and several hundred women. The age group of 26 to 35 is the second largest, with more than 900 men and more than 40 women. The age group under 15 is the third largest, with more than 230 men and more than 20 women. The age group of 36 to 45 is the fourth largest, with more than 90 men and more than 10 women. The age group over 45 is the smallest, with more than 10 men. In terms of occupation, shop assistants and apprentices are the most numerous, accounting for 37 percent. Students are the second most numerous, accounting for 38 percent. Next are company employees and engineers, followed by workers, and then the unemployed. Teachers are the least numerous. The total number of books borrowed last year was 200,8254 volumes, including 190,342 volumes from the checkout counter, 11,360 volumes borrowed from the reading room, and 6,552 volumes borrowed by mail from this and other cities. The highest number of visitors to the library last year was 529, and the lowest was 129. On average, the number of visitors was mostly between 300 and 400 per day. In terms of reading guidance, the library received more than 4,240 letters from this and other cities asking questions about books last year, which were answered successively, or publicly answered in Shenbao and Reading Life Bi-monthly. There are many other statistics in the library. It is reported that a commemorative album will be published soon and distributed to people from all walks of life and readers of the library, with detailed publication.

City News 157

▲The Invention of Domestic Gun Cleaning Oil

The oil used for guns and artillery in our country amounts to a huge number every year, and all of them are imported, which is very expensive. However, examining its raw materials, they are all exported from our country. The loss of rights and interests between import and export is countless. Someone who is well aware of the secrets of this has collected various raw materials and made Victory brand gun cleaning oil. Its quality is pure, it does not change in cold or heat, there is no residue, and its viscosity is qualified, which is comparable to foreign goods in every respect. It is even cheaper than foreign goods after lubrication. The application for the inspection certificate has been submitted to the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs. The head office is located at 80 Hualong Road, Shanghai, telephone 84817. There are two types of oil: one for military and police to clean guns and artillery, which is stored in large barrels, and each barrel is only half the price of foreign goods. The oil for self-defense pistols is stored in glass bottles, each bottle costs five dimes, with exquisite decoration and easy to carry.

Letters to the Editor 162

To Whom It May Concern:

We are writing on behalf of our clients, the creditors of China Industrial Bank, including Yu Ji, Nan Ji, Fu Ji, Ji Ji, Cheng Ji, Jin Ying Xian, and others. They have stated that they saw in your newspaper an article about the creditors' meeting of China Industrial Bank, in which the resolutions of the creditors were reported in a manner inconsistent with the facts.

According to our investigation, on January 26th of this month, a meeting of creditors of China Industrial Bank was held at the Chamber of Commerce. Nine creditor representatives, along with the defendant Lu Xihou and his legal representative Wu Linkun, were present. Lawyer Dong Yu first reported on the proceedings, after which Lu Xihou declared that at most, only 20% of the debt could be repaid after the final accounting. This contradicted his previous statement made during his detention, where he guaranteed the repayment of half of the debt. Moreover, his attitude was strong and his language was vulgar. He even threatened to voluntarily return to court and be detained again to coerce the creditors.

The creditors were extremely indignant at the time and insisted on maintaining the original plan. After the court clerk left, our clients and other creditors successively left the venue to devise a countermeasure in private. However, it was reported that after Lu Xihou left in disguise, the creditors suddenly agreed to Lu's proposed principle of repaying 20% of the debt and instructed Lu to publish a reply in the newspaper within two days. If this is not a fabricated publicity stunt, it is the result of manipulating a small number of creditors or representatives to create this illegal resolution, which is truly outrageous.

In addition to jointly petitioning the court to investigate and handle the matter according to law to protect our rights and interests, the matter concerns the overall interests of all creditors. We request that you, esteemed lawyers, send a letter of correction on behalf of the creditors to address the baseless resolutions reported in the newspaper, to clarify the facts and prevent manipulation by a few individuals.

We hereby inform you of the situation and respectfully request that you publish this letter in the "Letters to the Editor" section of your newspaper as a correction.

Respectfully,

*Shen Bao*

Lawyers: Shen Junru, Pan Ying, Zhuang Chengyi, Yu Zhongluo

January 28, 1934

Private Matter

Yesterday's Expanded Memorial Week City Mayor Wu's Report 163

Policy Directions for Shanghai Municipal Facilities in the Republic Year of 24

Fellow comrades, today is a most somber memorial day for Shanghai. Three years have passed since the January 28th Shanghai Incident. In these three years, thanks to the cooperation of local figures and the joint efforts of colleagues in the municipal government, the war zones of Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong, Zhenru, Dachang, and Miaohang have successively returned to their former appearance. Although Zhabei has not fully recovered, local figures and colleagues in the municipal government are currently working together to promote its restoration, which is expected in the near future. This is something to be gratified about.

However, in addition to our joy, we should also deeply investigate the reasons why we suffered such a catastrophe from the painful lessons left to us by this war. Of course, this is because our country's strength is insufficient. Therefore, the central government has declared to the whole country that we must enrich national strength and that local governments and people must work together to build up national strength. However, building national strength is a heavy responsibility with a long way to go. Other countries have achieved their current wealth and strength through a hundred and several decades of continuous effort. Our China is only beginning to build the country and enrich national strength today. If we still follow the construction procedures of other countries and do things step by step, it will take a hundred and several decades to achieve the same wealth and strength as other countries today. And by the time a hundred and several decades have passed, other countries will naturally have made even more progress than us. As a result, we will still be lagging behind. It can be seen that this kind of circuitous road is impassable. Because in today's international situation, we cannot afford to proceed slowly.

Therefore, the Premier told us to "catch up head-on." If our central and local governments and the 450 million compatriots across the country can unite and follow the Premier's last will to "catch up head-on" to build our country and enrich national strength, then perhaps in ten or eight years, our country will have a turning point.

Fellow comrades, we are all serving the city of Shanghai. Speaking of the city, today I will take Shanghai as an example. Let us make a comparative observation of the construction of the Shanghai concessions and the construction of the Shanghai urban area. The construction of the Shanghai concessions has a history of eighty or ninety years. The achievements shown by the orderly and relatively planned construction of the concessions over this long period of eighty or ninety years are only this. However, if we stick to conventions and follow their circuitous path, even to achieve the same construction as the concessions, I am afraid it will take us eighty or ninety years of effort, which would be too uneconomical. Therefore, we must now build our city in accordance with the Premier's last will and catch up head-on in order to achieve twice the result with half the effort. Shanghai is the largest city in China with a population of 3.45 million. To build Shanghai, we must first deeply understand what Shanghai lacks, what people did not pay attention to in the past, and strive to remedy it.

The Shanghai municipal construction of the past three years has several reportable characteristics. In the first year, we encountered the January 28th Incident, and most of our work was limited to responding to the war, handling post-war reconstruction in the war zone, and stabilizing social order. In the second year, we worked hard on the reconstruction of the war zone and continued to work hard on the active construction of the downtown area and the completion of the Shanghai Municipal Government Building. The third year, which was last year, we worked hard on cultural construction, such as libraries, museums, sports fields, gymnasiums, swimming pools, municipal hospitals, and other constructions that started one after another. Although some people criticized us, saying that this kind of construction could be postponed, or thought that it should be built in Nanshi or Zhabei, both of these criticisms have one-sided reasons. But taking the entire Shanghai as a whole, Shanghai is the largest city in China, a metropolis with a population of 3.45 million, and the above-mentioned constructions should exist. Not only should they exist, but they should have existed long ago. Let us take major Chinese cities such as Beijing, Guangzhou, and Nanjing as examples. Beijing today has only 1.12 million people, Guangzhou has only about one million people, Qingdao has only 500,000 people, Tianjin also has only 400,000 to 500,000 people, and Nanjing has only 700,000 people. However, all of the above-mentioned cities already have large libraries and large-scale sports fields. Shanghai, which calls itself the largest city in China, only has two libraries to this day, and both are very small, one in the concession and one in the Wenmiao in Nanshi. There is also only a small sports field in Nanshi. Speaking of hospitals, Shanghai, a metropolis with a population of 3.45 million, does not even have a municipal hospital. According to statistics, there are less than 2,000 hospital beds in the entire city of Shanghai. If we follow the public health facilities of foreign countries, it seems that there should be one hospital bed for every twenty people. Then how are these 2,000 hospital beds enough for Shanghai's population of 3.45 million? Based on this, libraries, museums, sports fields, gymnasiums, municipal hospitals, etc. are the most needed facilities in Shanghai at present. As for the reason why they should be built in the downtown area, it is naturally determined by the overall municipal construction plan. Any far-sighted municipal builder will be able to understand and agree. Moreover, the investment in the construction of the downtown area by the public and private sectors has reached 20 to 30 million yuan, which shows that the prosperity of the downtown area is not only a natural trend, but also a recent possible fact. This is a summary of the construction of this city in the past three years.

This year is the Republic Year of 24. What should we, the city government and I, strive for in the future? Regarding this point, I already have a message to the citizens on New Year's Day this year, which has been published in various newspapers. I believe that all comrades have seen it. Generally speaking, our construction this year has an important characteristic, which is social construction that is generally neglected by people but is related to the welfare of the majority of the people. China's current objective phenomenon is that everything is waiting to be done. However, we cannot do everything at once. We can only do what we can do. We will set a policy every year and carry out several construction projects step by step. Therefore, the policy direction for municipal facilities last year was cultural construction, while this year focuses on social construction. The construction of social undertakings in this city, including educational construction, can be divided into six aspects, which are now reported separately and briefly as follows:

(1) Building New Villages for the Common People: There are 150,000 to 200,000 compatriots in Shanghai who live in thatched sheds that are like hell. These compatriots in the slums are easy to be born and easy to die. The mortality rate is relatively high. Those who do not die often have diseases and live an inhuman life. We cannot bear to sit idly by and watch them drift along like this. We must rescue them from hell. Not only must we rescue them from hell, but we must also find ways to improve their lives so that they can also live a human life. First, we should first solve their housing problem. Therefore, the first task of the Shanghai Municipal Government this year is to build new villages for the common people to solve their housing problem. According to a rough estimate, there are about 30,000 thatched sheds in the entire city of Shanghai. Our current plan is to first build 10% of them, a total of 3,000 houses for the common people, with 500 houses as a new village. Each new village will have a school, which will also be a place for the common people to gather. Each new village will also have a simple clinic, a small-scale nursery, and a space for poor children to play. In addition, each new village will also have a public bathroom, which is separated for men and women, and a public place to wash clothes. All of these facilities are indispensable for their daily life. In this way, on the one hand, their housing problem is solved, and at the same time, their lives can be improved. Moreover, with the improvement of the lives of the common people, the resulting effects, hygiene, can also be further guaranteed. Because the source of diseases that are harmful to public health in the city is mostly in the slums. Therefore, if these slums are improved, the public health of our entire city and the health of the general public can be safely guaranteed. Therefore, building new villages for the common people is the most important social construction project of the Shanghai Municipal Government this year. This is what our colleagues should work together to achieve. (To be continued)

Small Western Paradise 164

—Written by Zhang Henshui

Eighth Episode: Remote Places, Light Officials, Far-Off, Strong-Willed Magistrate; Grand Hall, Lavish Banquet, Outside, Pitiful Insects

Let them force Bai, layer upon layer, pressing layer upon layer, hitting layer upon layer, hitting until the money is taken out to settle the matter. Zhang Jie went and said: This method is very poisonous, not afraid of not finding money. Zhou Yourong said: This was not invented now. They don't disturb the people; they let the county magistrate bear this great crime. They have left the Northwest, but this good method is still being used. Cheng Zhiqian smiled: County Magistrate Zhou is just so frank; he says everything. Zhou Yourong said: Xi'an is a place where there is national law. Why can't I say it? Also, they forced me, but I was unwilling to do it. Even if I did, I couldn't hand over two thousand silver in three days. Might as well die and compensate the people for a while. At that time, I said to my company commander, "Raising money is now the responsibility of the finance commissioner. You should ask him, don't ask me. If you are afraid of failing to complete the task, please ask your commander to come. The finance commissioner is also here. The three of us will talk face to face." That company commander had probably never encountered such a tough county magistrate since he started handling affairs. He immediately became enraged and raised his fist to hit me. Once he made a move, the brothers he brought along, why be polite, swarmed up and hit me without mercy, until I didn't even have the strength to cry "ouch." It was still a section chief by my side who shouted loudly, "You can't hit him! How will you explain to the province if you kill the county magistrate?" Perhaps they were trained. Hitting the county magistrate could only injure him, not kill him. Only after hearing these words did they spare me. From then on, I slept in bed for two weeks. While I was recuperating in bed, I thought to myself, "With a five-foot body, where can't I find a bowl of rice to eat? Why suffer such torture?" After another half month, I asked for leave to go to the province. Before leaving, I was still worried that they would detain me. (124)

Red Sheep Trivial Talks 165

— Zheng Yimei

The Red Sheep story has already been performed on stage, and now Xinhua Film Company is filming a sound movie to promote the national spirit, which is a very good intention. I will now describe what I know about the trivial matters of the Taiping Army to provide some help for discussion.

The clothing and colors of the Taiping Army are a matter of contention among those who study stage plays. Most people generally believe that they wore red turbans and red clothes. Some say that the turbans and uniforms of the Taiping Army were all yellow. Forty years ago, the *Iron Rooster* performed also had yellow turbans, but later the authenticity was gradually lost. However, according to the *Abridged Record of the Pacification of the Guangdong Bandits*, "The bandits favored yellow in their clothing. The pseudo-kings all wore yellow robes, embroidered with dragons, and their crowns were also like this. Those below the pseudo-marquises also wore yellow robes, while those below the pseudo-commanders wore red robes. Their jackets and short-sleeved back clothing were embroidered with dragons and phoenixes, done arbitrarily without a fixed system. Both men and women wrapped their heads with long scarves, with the ends dragging to their hips. Pseudo-division commanders and above used yellow, while those below used red. Whether silk or cloth, it was all up to them. Many were red inside, so the people of Jianghuai called the bandits 'Red Heads,' and their hoods were also red." From this, it can be seen that yellow was the clothing of the upper ranks, and red was the clothing of the lower ranks, and the contentions can be resolved.

After Hong Xiuquan established his capital in Jiangning, he summoned the English craftsman Ross and the Hong Kong worker Zhou Bin to supervise the manufacture of six types of gold and silver coins to trade with Western countries. The large gold coin was 5 pounds, the medium gold coin was 2 pounds, and the small gold coin was 1 pound. Each pound was made into ten large silver coins, the large silver coin was 100 cents, the medium silver coin was 50 cents, and the small silver coin was 20 cents. The weight and size were all modeled after the Hong Kong gold and silver coins. However, although the gold and silver coins were made, they could not be circulated. Because Western countries regarded the Heavenly Kingdom as an unofficial state, they uniformly refused to use them, and Hong Tianwang destroyed them all in anger. Those who secretly kept them regarded them as treasures. Someone who saw them said that the front of the coin was inscribed with "Taiping Heavenly Kingdom," and the back was horizontally inscribed with "Jin Bin" in seal script. Also, the Taiping copper coins had "Taiping Heavenly Kingdom" inscribed on the front and "Sheng Bin" in regular script on the back, either arranged vertically or horizontally.

The names of the figures in the Taiping Army were often changed to avoid taboos. After being used for a long time, the original names were forgotten, so I have recorded them below: Li Xiucheng's original name was Yiwen, and the Heavenly King changed his name to Xiucheng. Yang Xiuqing's original name was Sizaijing. Wei Changhui's original name was Zheng. Chen Yucheng's original name was Picheng, and the Heavenly King praised his achievements and changed his name to Yucheng. Zeng Tianyang's original name was Tianyang, but to avoid the Heavenly King's name, he changed Tian to Tian. Huang Zaixing's original name was Tianshen, also to avoid the character Tian, so he changed his name to Zaixing. Zeng Fengchuan's original name was Jin. Huang Yiyun's original name was Yiyun, but to avoid the taboo of Nanfeng, he changed his name to Yiyun. Chen Qishi's original name was Qishi. Li Junliang's original name was Junchang, but to avoid the taboo of Beiwei, he changed his name to Junliang. Lu Xianba's original name was Xianda, but to avoid the taboo of Shi Dakai, he changed his name to Xianba. Li Laifang's original name was Kaifang, but to avoid the taboo of Yi Shi, his name was changed to Laifang in all documents and reports. Li Laisheng's original name was Kaisheng, and he also changed his name to avoid the taboo of Yi Shi.

Tidbits 166

—(Chen Yunsu)

There's a saying: "No cat doesn't eat fish, no official doesn't want gold." I think the saying that no cat doesn't eat fish is quite believable, but as for the saying that no official doesn't want gold, I absolutely deny it. Why? Because isn't every official swearing to be honest and content with simplicity when they take office? How can they overthrow themselves and slap themselves in the face?

Returning from Listening to Storytelling in the Countryside 167

—Xunzi

Storytelling is a local art of Suzhou with mass appeal. The three prefectures of Hangjiahu along the Huhang Railway, as well as Changzhou and below along the Huning Railway, and many towns in the Taihu Lake basin, are all areas where the famous artists of Guangyu Society are active.

In the past year or two, radio has become popular, and several leading figures and top performers of Guangyu Society have abandoned the storytelling stage and switched to broadcasting stations. However, only the propertied and leisured classes can afford to buy radios. As for the small teahouses in thatched huts in the countryside, where many mud-legged villagers gather, quietly waiting for the storyteller to take the stage, a piece of sounding wood and a stringed instrument are gifts to comfort the toiling masses. Storytelling there is a true mass art. Although the storyteller's remuneration is meager, its value far exceeds that of the so-called famous storytellers who only serve the leisured ladies and gentlemen at broadcasting stations. However, it is said that those who have not become famous, or who have recently graduated, are willing to go to small wharves to sing and tell stories. As for those who have become famous, they swear that they will never run the wharves again.

This time, I had the opportunity to listen to a storytelling performance on a small wharf along the Luhuning Railway. The ballad was "Jade Dragonfly," and the story was "Tales of the Martyrs." The storyteller was certainly not among the famous artists, and besides, whether it was a long story or a short story, it was full of feudal colors. "Jade Dragonfly" and "Tales of the Martyrs" naturally could not escape the shackles of the era. However, the description of the nuns of the Fahua Nunnery, breaking through the barriers of etiquette and achieving sexual satisfaction, how bold was that in the beginning? The second half tells the story of Jin Zhang's usurpation, saying that Jin Zhang was known as the tigress of Suzhou.

This, in the originally male-centered society, was nothing less than a bold act of giving women a voice. Therefore, I believe that if "Jade Dragonfly" is re-evaluated, it is indeed much higher than the "Fallen Golden Fan," which does not escape the clichés of the talented scholar and beautiful lady, and the feudal remnants of the "Pearl Pagoda" and so on. In Shanghai, Zhang Yunting, who tells "Jade Dragonfly," seems to be blown down by the wind when he steps down from the stage. However, when he is on the stage, he is energetic. He is a typical figure of an artist. I like listening to his stories the most!

"Tales of the Martyrs" is just a narration of the history of the Ming Taizu's founding of the country. This kind of autocratic tyrant who uses killing as power has no value to worship! However, just discussing the story, Jiang Yifei can tell the story clearly. Compared to interspersing one or two current events, which is considered "yin xue," in my personal opinion, he is better than the former!

After fifteen years of division, it is now returned. Patriots should protect their borders like this.

Fragrant Shadows: A Record 170

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Finally, someone told Li Lianying about my actions in the Imperial Ancestral Temple. This person certainly wouldn't let the matter rest! He secretly told the Empress Dowager: "This fire started very strangely! It is said that when the Emperor was performing the sacrifice, he actually imitated the foreign soldiers and gave a hand salute. No wonder the ancestors were angered!" Thus, she became furious after dawn and severely scolded me, as if the fire in the Imperial Ancestral Temple was all my fault. Don't you think this is a joke?"

I had never heard of this matter before, but I didn't feel like making any comment. I could only use a smile as a way out.

The Empress Dowager's temper was really very strange! No matter what she did, she always couldn't avoid regretting it. Although she had listened to the words of the two officials of the Imperial Observatory and decided to cancel the plan to continue heading east, she was extremely eager for the scenery of the Changbai Mountains and deeply regretted not doing the calculation. She suspected that their calculations might not be accurate, and maybe tomorrow would be the most auspicious day. Wouldn't she have missed it in vain? However, how could she risk such a great danger (?)? Because she dared not risk getting involved, but could not forget the original plan, she felt an indescribable annoyance herself. Because of her annoyance, the people of the entire palace were affected, making us all feel extremely bored and uneasy. The entire ancient palace of Shengjing was shrouded in an atmosphere of melancholy. I think we won't be able to see happy scenes again before we return to Beijing! (234)

Local Customs and Minor Records

The Development of Shanghai Hospitals (Part 1) 171

— Shanghai News Agency

The history of hospitals in Shanghai can be divided into two periods: The first is the period of establishment by foreigners, which includes two phases: "Establishment by Churches" and "Establishment by Foreign Public and Concession Authorities." The second period is the period of self-establishment by Chinese, which also has two phases: the first is "Publicly Run," and the second is "Municipally Run."

After Shanghai opened as a port, Christian and Catholic missionaries, with the permission of treaties, flocked here to make it a center for missionary work; at the same time, they began their medical endeavors, which were very helpful in assisting their missionary activities. In another sense, it brought a new public health system and methods to this place. This kind of social welfare work carried out by the churches has become a glorious record in history and is not easily forgotten by the people. The names often on their lips are:

Renji Hospital 1843 Established by the London Missionary Society

Lester Chinese Hospital later Shandong

Road Hospital

Tongren Hospital 1867 Established by the American Episcopal Church

St. Luke's Hospital

Women and Children's Hospital 1885 Established by the Women's Missionary Society

Margaret Williamson Hospital

Guangren Hospital 1903 Established by the American Episcopal Church

St. Elizabeth Hospital

Guangci Hospital 1904 Established by the Catholic Church

Hospital St. Marie

Renji Hospital was the first hospital in Shanghai, founded by Dr. Wm. Lockhar, a priest of the London Missionary Society. He came to Shanghai in 1843 and began his preaching work in the city. At that time, Shanghai had just been declared open as a commercial port, and the residential area for foreigners had not yet been delineated. His hospital was initially located in the South Gate and moved to the outer city of the North Gate in 1846. In 1844, he bought 24 acres of land south of present-day Shandong Road and Fuzhou Road for 45 yuan per mu as the center of the London Missionary Society. The land price there has now risen to 35,000 taels of silver per mu. In 1861, Renji Hospital began selling real estate outside the North Gate and built a hospital on Shandong Road. This hospital did many things, so that most people in Shanghai knew what was called "Ma Jia Quan" - this is the local name for the London Missionary Society. How did the London Missionary Society get called Ma Jia Quan? The reason is that the first Protestant missionary to come to China was Dr. Morrison. The locals pronounced the sound of the word "Mo" as the character "Mai." They saw that the area of Renji Hospital had become a gathering place for missionaries, so they called it Ma Jia Quan. (Note) The management rights of this hospital were later transferred to the committee of local social organizations, while the London Missionary Society provided doctors, nurses, and staff, and retained missionary work. It has become a public and religious hospital.

Not long ago, it received a grant of two million taels from the Lester legacy fund and was rebuilt into the most modern hospital. The English name of the hospital was also changed from "Shandong Road Hospital" to "Lester Chinese Hospital" in memory.

The establishment of Tongren Hospital is also an exciting story. Initially, there was an American woman living in Shanghai, Mrs. E. Shields, who suffered from a severe eye disease. She sought treatment from a Christian doctor and recovered. The doctor refused payment, so Mrs. Xi donated 100 US dollars and instructed Thomson, a clergyman of the Episcopal Church, to use it to help the poor. Tang consulted with Wu Hongyu, a Chinese clergyman, about the use of the money. Wu said, "There are too many poor people in Shanghai. It is impossible to save them all with a hundred dollars. If we use these hundred dollars for medical expenses to save the poor and sick, wouldn't that be better?" Tang clapped his hands in praise. Therefore, they rented a house for six yuan a month as a pharmacy. For a time, foreign doctors in the area came to the pharmacy to provide diagnosis and treatment. Wu Hongyu, in his spare time from preaching, raised funds for the hospital, so that this small-scale pharmacy would not be abandoned halfway, and there would be surplus funds to accumulate. Coincidentally, someone wanted to sell thirteen old houses in the Hongkou area. Wu and Tang bought it and combined it into eleven bays, and the signboard of "Tongren Hospital" was inscribed at this time, several years after the initial creation.

Educational News

Citizens' Education Center Commemorates January 28th 172

Yesterday was the third anniversary of January 28th. The Shanghai Municipal Public Education Center held a solemn memorial meeting in the lecture hall at 9:00 a.m. yesterday. Five to six hundred citizens attended, presided over by Chen Songchun, the director of the center.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Troop to Hold Memorial for Four Martyred Members 173

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Troop participated in the Songhu Anti-Japanese War work and was falsely accused of being spies by the enemy. The members Luo Yunxiang, Ying Wenda, Mao Zhengxiang, and Bao Zhengwu were brutally killed. At that time, because the enemy was afraid of being sanctioned by world justice, they destroyed the corpses. In order to commemorate the four martyrs, the troop built a memorial tomb in the Shanghai Cemetery in Jiangwan, which will be completed soon. In addition to building a memorial tower for the four martyrs in front of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Auditorium at Tianhougong Bridge, the troop will convene all normal and reserve members of the three armies every year on the anniversary of the martyrdom of the four martyrs to hold a memorial meeting. This month, the 31st is the third anniversary of the martyrdom of the four martyrs. The troop has ordered all faculty and staff members and the families of the four martyrs to gather at the headquarters to hold a three-week memorial ceremony, lower the flag to half-mast, and suspend training for one day. Lianhua Film Company will also bring two films of the memorial service for the four martyrs and the two-week memorial service for screening.

Zhejiang Education Director Xu Talks About the Issue of Changing the Education Bureau to a Section 174

After Huang Shaoxiong took office as the chairman of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, he was determined to reform county administration. There was a saying that he would raise the authority of the county magistrate based on the Lanchi Experimental County method, save county administrative expenses, and merge various bureaus under the county into sections. The County Education Bureau is also among those to be merged. Xu Shaodi, the director of the Education Department, said to people yesterday that all administration must be unified in authority and clearly defined in responsibilities, which is what I have always advocated. I strongly agree that county administration should adopt a centralized system. However, regarding the matter of changing the Education Bureau to a section, in the current situation, advantages and disadvantages are seen. In the future, whether to conduct experiments in a small number of counties first and then decide on a unified method is still under study. It is noted that the Education Bureaus of various counties are roughly equivalent to the persuasion offices of the Qing Dynasty. After the revolution, they were either established or abolished. During the Republic of China, a special section was set up in the county office to manage education. By the fourth year of the Republic of China, due to the complexity of local education and the inability to focus on responsibilities, it was difficult to promote, so the persuasion offices were restored. It was not until the eleventh year of the Republic of China that the persuasion offices were changed to education bureaus. Recently, after a part of Jiangsu Province changed its methods, Shandong also decided to change the bureau to a section at the provincial education administration meeting. As for the bandit suppression provinces, because the provincial government adopted a joint office system, the counties also followed the camp order to uniformly change the bureau to a section. If this proposition is also realized in our province, then the county office will set up a section to manage the educational administrative affairs of the entire county, which will be similar to the political system of the early Republic of China. Currently, there are roughly two reasons for advocating changing the bureau to a section: one is to save expenses, and the other is to increase the authority of the county magistrate. Changing the bureau to a section can reduce educational administrative expenses, and this kind of savings can be used to subsidize local educational undertakings. However, in terms of the province, we must pay attention to the fact that after the section is changed, the expenses will not only not be reduced, but must be increased quite a bit. It is found that the administrative expenses of the Education Bureau of the entire county are estimated to be more than 380,000 yuan, of which more than 80,000 yuan are subsidized by the province, and the remaining 290,000 yuan are local education funds. It is also found that the treatment of personnel in the Education Bureau is very different from that of personnel in the county government. The treatment of personnel in the education sector is meager, and the salary of the director of the bureau is equal to that of a section member or clerk in the county government. After the bureau is changed, the treatment of the section chief and school supervisor will naturally be the same as that of other section chiefs and section members. Therefore, although the number of personnel is reduced, the salary will increase instead, and the provincial subsidy will inevitably increase. Therefore, the frugality of expenses is a one-sided view. As for the improvement of the authority of the county magistrate, special attention should be paid, that is, if education is handled by a section, the selection of county magistrate candidates should be strictly screened. Recent inspections and reports show that many county magistrates pay attention to the development of education, but there are also many who despise it and do not take education seriously at all. There are countless examples. It is no different than trying to catch fish by climbing a tree to expect these people to be able to promote local educational undertakings. Therefore, to realize the plan to change the bureau to a section, the selection of county magistrate candidates must be screened first.

Ministry of Education Promotes Simplified Characters, Li and Wang Arrive in Shanghai Yesterday to Investigate Copper Molds 177

▲Li talked in detail about casting phonetic copper molds and simplified characters

▲The Chinese Stenography Society is scheduled to invite Wang to give a lecture on stenography

In order to make compulsory education and public education easier to promote, the Ministry of Education has specially decided to compile a simplified character spectrum and cast copper molds for phonetic Chinese characters, and sent Li Jinxi and Wang Yi of the National Language Unification Preparatory Committee to Shanghai to investigate copper molds. They arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning. A reporter from the Shanghai News Agency specially visited them yesterday. According to the talk, the details are as follows:

Overview of the work of the National Language Council Li first talked about the National Language Unification Preparatory Committee, which was established in the eighth year of the Republic of China and reorganized once in the seventeenth year. Thirty-one commissioners were publicly hired, with Wu Zhihui as the chairman of the commission, and Qian Xuantong, Lu Maozhi, Li Jinxi and other seven people as standing commissioners. The main work over the years is divided into: ㈠ Unification, such as agreeing on the standard of national language and national language, and adopting standard vocabulary and grammar. ㈡ Legislation, such as agreeing on phonetic symbols and various symbols related to national language literature. ㈡ Review, such as reviewing books on national language and national pronunciation, and inspecting and correcting the teaching of national language and national pronunciation. ㈣ Documents, such as historical investigation, collection, collation, statistics, and commendation. As for the planned activities, they are described in detail in the Outline of the History of the National Language Movement, which was recently published by Commercial Press. The Chinese Dictionary and the National Language Romanization are roughly larger-scale works.

Casting phonetic Chinese copper molds Next, the National Language Unification Association decided to set up a National Language Printing House at the seventh regular meeting in January this year. The purpose is to cast the entire lead-character copper mold with phonetic symbols next to Chinese characters, and it was decided that this copper mold should be cast and promoted by the state. Therefore, the meeting submitted a case to the ministry to allocate funds for casting. Wang Shijie, the Minister of Education, sent a letter to Li Jinxi and Wang Yi on January 15, inviting various members of the meeting to discuss the actual plan in detail and bring it to Beijing for discussion. The colleagues arrived in Beijing on the 23rd and held a meeting at the Ministry of Education on the 26th. It was decided to send the colleagues to Shanghai first to investigate the copper mold. It will take about a week to complete. In the future, the Ministry of Education may issue an order that popular reading materials, elementary school textbooks, and newspaper columns should all be printed with this lead type.

The Ministry of Education compiles a simplified character spectrum Since the National Language Unification Association passed the reduction of the strokes of existing Chinese characters in the eleventh year of the Republic of China, it organized the Chinese Character Simplified Committee and elected Qian Xuantong, Hu Shi, Li Jinxi and other fifteen people as commissioners. At that time, due to the unsettled situation, it was unable to proceed. Last year, it passed the collection of inherent and more applicable simplified characters and decided to compile a simplified character spectrum. Later, Chen Guangyao, a member of the Xijing Preparatory Committee, requested Chairman Jiang to promote simplified characters. The Ministry of Education issued an order to the National Language Council to quickly review and report it, and to propose detailed opinions on promoting simplified characters to assist public education for verification. After the National Language Council reviewed and reported it to the ministry, the ministry invited colleagues to Beijing to discuss it together with the previous case. As a result, it was decided to first complete the practical simplified character spectrum, which was the responsibility of seven commissioners, and then the ministry would officially announce it or order public education reading materials and textbooks to be used uniformly.

The situation of promoting national language shorthand Wang Yi, the inventor of Chinese National Language Shorthand, said, "Thirty years ago, I realized that Chinese pronunciation can be performed in a simple way in the "Old Empty Valley Method", but at that time, the pronunciation was mostly based on the southern dialect, so it was not widely used. After arriving in the north, I studied the national language and compiled and printed the Chinese New Stenography Technique in the eighth year of the Republic of China. I have revised it several times based on my teaching experience at the Beijing Stenography Training Institute. I have ordered a one-character, one-line Wang Yi Stenography, and the National Language Unification Association of the Ministry of Education has opened a National Language Stenography Training Institute in Beijing, Nanjing and other places, for a total of fifteen sessions. Although I am here to investigate copper molds, I intend to take this opportunity to contact teaching classes in Shanghai. Learning shorthand is not difficult, it just requires persistence."

The Stenography Society invites Wang to give a lecture The Chinese Stenography Society has been working very hard since it was founded by Zhu Zhongzheng, He Zhen, Wang Gongxia, Chen Dongbai, Zhu Zhiming and others. For example, the Tenth Professor Cultural Construction Symposium and the Vocational Education Society Experts Meeting were all recorded by the association, with good results. Now that Wang Yi, the inventor of Chinese Stenography, has come to Shanghai, he will give a lecture on Chinese Stenography at 7:30 p.m. on the 31st of this month (Thursday) on the third floor of the Baxian Overseas Chinese Youth Association. Members and non-members are welcome to attend.

Plays Not Reviewed Are Not Allowed to Be Performed 182

▲The Municipal Education Bureau ordered the Lake Society, etc. to comply

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau yesterday instructed the Lake Society, the Ningbo Shanghai Fellow Association, the Central Auditorium, and various theaters, cinemas, and public and private secondary schools and above in the city, stating that all operas performed in the city should comply with the provisions of Article 3 of the bureau's regulations on the review of opera records. An application form should be prepared in advance, and two copies of the opera content, explanation or script, and actor name list should be submitted to the bureau for review. Only after approval can rehearsals be held. It is now found that various drama groups in the city borrow schools or cinemas and other public places to perform dramas, often without complying with the legal procedures, which is inappropriate. It is hereby ordered that the theaters and schools should absolutely not allow drama groups to borrow venues if their scripts have not been reviewed and approved by the bureau.

The Municipal Education Association Continues to Run Civil Schools 183

▲Scheduled to start school on March 1

▲Huang Zhaoxiong will serve as the principal

The Shanghai Municipal Education Association has spared no effort in promoting social education in the city for the past two years. It has run as many as 22 civil schools. The association believes that there are many illiterate people in the local area. Running civil schools can achieve great results with very little funding. Therefore, the board of directors decided to continue running the original First Civil School, and it will start enrolling students on March 1 and will be run permanently. With reduced funding, the restrictions on students are stricter than before. Huang Zhaoxiong, a standing director, will serve as the principal concurrently. Mr. Huang is very willing to sacrifice some of his energy and time to make an effort to make the school a model civil school.

膠州路檳榔路潘園私立上海幼稚師範學校、爲全國幼稚師資唯一訓練之所、年來學生激增、除借附近滬西醫院三層樓洋房爲宿舍外、尙感不敷應用、去年秋間、於潘園南部添建新樓十二幢、業已工竣、朱欄畫棟、輪奐聿新、將作爲師範生息修之所云、 184

The private Shanghai Kindergarten Normal School on Jiaozhou Road, Pinlang Road, and Pan Garden is the only training place for kindergarten teachers in the country. In recent years, the number of students has surged. In addition to borrowing a three-story foreign-style building from the nearby Huxi Hospital as a dormitory, it is still felt that it is not enough. Last autumn, twelve new buildings were added to the south of Pan Garden, and the construction has been completed. The red railings and painted beams are brand new and will be used as a place for normal school students to live and study.

The famous tennis player Gorge of the family passed away

（哈瓦斯社二十七日紐約電）世界著名網球家戈爾傑、今日在紐約州馬格萊脫維爾城逝世、享年四十六歲、按戈爾傑前曾獲得世界網球錦標、並於一九○六年、一九○七年、二九○八年、一九一四年、迭獲英國網球錦標、近患喉頸炎症、已歷數星期、卒致不起、其父爲美國鐵路業巨擘、戈爾傑（姓）喬治（名）氏、爲其第二子、其祖老戈爾傑、當其初來美國時、囊中僅携美元數枚、及捕鼠器一具、賴經營得法、乃致發跡、今茲小戈爾傑傳祖父遺業、以億萬钜　終其天年云、

(Havas News Agency, New York, 27th) Gorge, a world-renowned tennis player, passed away today in Margaretville, New York, at the age of 46. Gorge had previously won the World Tennis Championship and won the British Tennis Championship repeatedly in 1906, 1907, 2908, and 1914. He recently suffered from throat and neck inflammation, which lasted for several weeks and eventually led to his death. His father was a giant in the American railway industry. Gorge (surname), George (name), was his second son. His grandfather, the old Gorge, only carried a few dollars and a mousetrap when he first came to the United States. Relying on good management, he became rich. Now the younger Gorge inherited his grandfather's legacy and ended his life with billions of dollars.

New Record for Women's 100m Backstroke

（哈瓦斯社二十七日荷蘭京城電）荷蘭著名游泳家馬斯登勃魯克女士、本日在此間以一分十六秒六之時間、游畢一百公尺背泳、較其本人於去年十一月二十五日在德國杜塞爾道夫城所造成之世界新紀錄、尤少五分之一秒、按百公尺背泳世界紀錄、原爲美國霍爾姆女士所保持、其速度爲一分十八秒三、至去年爲馬女士以一分十六秒八之速度所打破、今則馬女士又復打破其自己所造成之世界紀錄云、

(Havas News Agency, The Hague, Netherlands, 27th) The famous Dutch swimmer Ms. Marsden Brook swam the 100-meter backstroke in 1 minute and 16.6 seconds today, which is 1/5 of a second faster than the new world record she set in Dusseldorf, Germany on November 25 last year. According to the world record for the 100-meter backstroke, it was originally held by Ms. Holm of the United States, whose speed was 1 minute and 18.3 seconds. Last year, Ms. Ma broke it with a speed of 1 minute and 16.8 seconds. Today, Ms. Ma broke her own world record again.

（哈瓦斯社二十七日美國芝加哥電）美國女游泳家霍爾姆女士、原爲百公尺背泳世界紀錄保持者、至去年十一月二十五日、爲荷蘭女游泳家馬斯登勃魯克女士、所打破、今日馬女士在荷蘭京城又以一分十六秒八、打破其自己所造成之世界紀錄、同時霍女士在此間以一分十六秒三、游畢百公尺背泳、結果世界最新紀錄、卒爲霍女士所奪得云、

(Havas News Agency, Chicago, USA, 27th) The American female swimmer Ms. Holm was originally the world record holder for the 100-meter backstroke. On November 25th last year, it was broken by the Dutch female swimmer Ms. Marsden Brook. Today, Ms. Ma broke her own world record again with 1 minute and 16.8 seconds in The Hague, Netherlands.
